************* TODO Kraskov MI confidence intervals using m out of n bootstrap
              :properties:
              :id:       d104d4d3-c0c2-4981-906c-38fc045a42f2
              :end:

              necessary for knn-mi estimator b/c bootstrap w/ replacement screws up
              Kraskov MI Estimator.  see [[File:~/work/dtu/doc/energy.bib::francois06permtestmutinf][Francois et al. 2006]] MI perm test.

*************** [[subsampling bootstrap (m out of n bootstrap)]]
*************** [[http://cscs.umich.edu/~crshalizi/notabene/bootstrap-entropy.html][doubt]] about whether bootstrapping works for entropy, etc.

                from the page:

                  why might this not work? suppose x is binary, and both outcomes are
                  equally likely. then h[x] = 1, which is the maximum value. hence
                  empirical entropies will be less than or equal to the true
                  entropy. suppose our empirical distribution has less than maximum
                  entropy, i.e., it's not completely fair. but if we resample the
                  empirical distribution, it may chance that the sample is more nearly
                  fair than the original. so the resampled entropy can be higher than
                  the estimate, while the estimate cannot be higher than the true
                  entropy. but it could be, of course, that the two distributions do
                  approach each other, in some limiting sense which i might have to
                  think carefully about.

                he has a couple "to reads" that might be relevant.
************* TODO picking Kraskov k

              [[file:energy.bib::Maier10clustNhbds][Maier 2010: Clustering]] KNN-Rnn spectral clustering, # clusters
              (kraskov must pick KNN k)

              [[file:~/work/dtu/doc/energy.bib::francois07resampparamfreefeatsel][francois et al. 2007: resampling]] has a featsel bootstrap trick, maybe
              can't use.  but it, and others, say that bias increases w/ k; variance
              decreases.  if have too much data, then running on a lot of random subsets
              (chosen w/o replacement so bootstrap doesn't screw up the knn mi est.)
              then have mean and also a variance estimate.  not sure how low to go,
              though.

              could somehow pick k assuming data is multivariate gaussian: compute
              mean/var, then have theoretical information (in one of the mi papers,
              it has the cov matrix, not just r).  the pick k to match this
              theoretical mi on the gaussian data?  normal dist is minimal entropy
              dist w/ 2 moments, or something like that, right?

              bias is a funciton of k/npts for 2d: [[file:~/work/dtu/doc/energy.bib::kraskov04estmutinfknn][kraskov et al. 2004:
              estimating]], fig 4.  they like k=2-4 when not looking for zero-valued
              strict dependence.

            <<Mutual Information Properties>>
************* mi independence additivity

                i(x,w;,y,z) = i(x;y) + i(w;z)  when [xy] indep. [wz]

                from: [[http://www.scholarpedia.org/article/mutual_information][scholarpedia: mutual information]]

************* mi data processing inequality: post-processing cannot increase information
              <<mi data processing inequality>>

              if z is a function of y _only_, then:

                i(x;z)≤i(x;y).

              i.e. if z is an estimate of x obtained from y (e.g. linear
              regression of y upon x), then the linear regression residuals
              are a lower bound of i(x;y).

************* [[http://www.mtm.ufsc.br/~taneja/book/node6.html][entropy properties]] (wikipedia has some too).
************* multi-dimensional mi bounds
              <<multi-dimensional mi bounds>>

            could use these indepenence assumption to lower bound some mi
            decomposition intended to reduce the dimensionality bias in the
            kraskov estimator (see ramps.org).  if vars are indepedendent
            then can sum.  if not, then, since mi is pos. (check when this is
            true for multi-dim mi b/c i was confused about that) then the
            extra mi due to presence of unmodeled dependence can only add.
            so, a decompostion that assumes independence is a lower bound,
            right?

            is there a way to upper bound it?
            limited

            [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/inequalities_in_information_theory][inequalities in information theory]]
            [[file:energy.bib::][Asari 2005: Technical Notes Linear]] (upper and lower MI bounds, for Gaussians, I think)

********* Transfer Entropy
          <<Transfer Entropy>>

          It's like R^2 for an information theoretic ARX filter: It's
          information about the output contained in its history and the
          history of other external conditioning variables.  So could
          pick autoregressive NN inputs and their lags.

*********** [[https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transfer_entropy][Wikipedia]] definition:

          Transfer entropy is conditional mutual information,[4][5] with the
          history of the influenced variable

            {\displaystyle Y_{t-1:t-L}} Y_{t-1:t-L}

          in the condition.

*********** good intro: [[file:energy.bib::Wibral15BitsBrainsTE][Wibral et al. 2015: Bits Brains Biologically Inspired Computing]] ()
*********** [[file:energy.bib::Lizier12compNetsTransEnt][Lizier et al. 2012: Multivariate]] constr. TE

******* Partial Mutual Information Feature Selection
        <<Partial Mutual Information Feature Selection>>

        MI between features and output is maybe the ultimate for
        nonlinear feature selection: it approximates Bayes error rate
        which means that min error will be achieved when there is max
        I(Y,features) [[file:energy.bib::May11revVarSelNN][May et al. 2011: Review]].

        Full MI calc is better for featsel than pairwise MI
        estimation (e.g. mRMR: peng05featSelMutInfo) because pairwise
        techniques don't compare output-variable-specific redundancy
        or truly capture feature synergy
        ([[file:energy.bib::Wang14featSelChemMI][Wang et al. 2014: Feature Selection Chemical)]]. But
        bruteforce search for max MI, as in Wang14, above is
        computationally combinatoric in the # of possible features --
        not doable for high dimensions.

        _Partial MI feature selection_ is an incremental stepwise
        search that avoids combinatorial search while still
        maximizing full feature/output mutual information, because MI
        can be factored into sums of partial MI
        ([[file:energy.bib::May11revVarSelNN][May et al. 2011: Review of featsel]]).  PMI handles redundancy
        and synergy that pairwise techniques try to handle; PMI (or
        conditional MI) _removes redundancy and adds synergy_, so its
        conditioned result can be _bigger or smaller_ than
        unconditioned MI ([[file:energy.bib::Lizier14JIDTinfoToolkit_SupMat][Lizier 2014: Supplementary Material]]).  This
        is a greedy search: [[file:energy.bib::Lizier12compNetsTransEnt][Lizier et al. 2012: Multivariate]] explains
        shortcomings, has some (obvious) fixes.

        PMI estimation type:

        _kNN multivariate PMI_: the efficient MI estimation method in
        [[file:energy.bib::Kraskov04EstMutInfKNN][Kraskov et al. 2004: Estimating]] has been modifed to do PMI in
        [[file:energy.bib::Frenzel07partMutInfo][Frenzel & Pompe 2007: Partial Mutual Information]].  This would
        seem to be the ideal because everything would be done without
        a regression algorithm in the middle (as with a wrapper),
        thus making very few assumptions (mainy the KNN k).  However,
        there would still be a high dim PMI calc if there really were
        a high # of relevant features (but not if there aren't since
        it's incremental, starting w/ most important features and w/ a
        stopping criteria).  I don't know how problematic this is b/c
        I haven't seen a paper on it and I can't find a working
        implementation of this algorithm (but see [[Partial Mutual Information Code]]).
        Another implementation of this idea, [[file:energy.bib::Kugiumtzis13directCplngPMI][Kugiumtzis 2013: Direct]]
        Finally, [[file:energy.bib::Vlachos10nonUnifStSpcMI][Vlachos & Kugiumtzis 2010: Nonuniform]] shows how kNN
        PMI/CMI has less dimension-dependent bias than kNN MI, as used in
        ([[file:energy.bib::Wang14featSelChemMI][Wang et al. 2014: Feature Selection Chemical)]]

        Note that straighforward kNN PMI techniques don't work for discrete outputs b/c MI is not defined in these cases ([[cite:Ross14MutInfoCntnAndDscrt][Ross 2014: Mutual Information Discrete]]).  Ross14 has a workaround, and [[cite:Lizier14JIDTinfoToolkit][Lizier 2014: JIDT]]
        has an experimental function for this mixed continuous/discrete (as of Dec. 2016).
        _1D MI and embedded regression_: Multivariate PMI can also be
        estimated with single dimension MI if candFeat|selectedFeats
        is estimated with single regression, as in [[file:energy.bib::May08varSelpartMutInfo][May et al. 2008: Non]].
        This would avoid the high dim MI/PMI estimation problem,
        would be easy to implement, and can handle high dims e.g.
        500 in [[file:energy.bib::May08partMutInfoWaterFrcst][May et al. 2008: Application ANN]]. But you still have
        to fiddle with a lot of regressions in the selection loop;
        comment in [[file:energy.bib::Frenzel07partMutInfo][Frenzel & Pompe 2007: Partial Mutual Information]]
        says kNN PMI is "lower complexity"

        KNN+KDE: [[File:energy.bib::may08varselpartmutinfo][May et al. 2008: non linear variable]]
        KNN+KDE: [[File:energy.bib::may08partmutinfowaterfrcst][May et al. 2008: application of partial]] (500 variable
             candidates, does lags)
        KNN: [[file:energy.bib::Kugiumtzis13directCplngPMI][Kugiumtzis 2013: Direct]]
        KNN: [[file:energy.bib::Vlachos10nonUnifStSpcMI][Vlachos & Kugiumtzis 2010: Nonuniform]]
        KDE: [[file:energy.bib::Dalto14NshrtWindFrcstNNpmi][DHalto et al. 2014: Neural]]

Joseph Lizier <joseph.lizier@gmail.com>
Jul 20 2016 (1 day ago)

to JIDT
Hi Scott,

Ok, I see what you're saying.

If you really want to get at those terms in eq 11/12, it could be done by
making some hacks/modifications yourself to our KSG conditional MI
calculator. It's a little complicated but I outline those below.

But before I do, let me reiterate that the method I'm suggesting as best
practise -- statistical testing of the conditional MI itself -- uses a
single measure which doesn't change for different kinds of data, and the
stopping threshold (as a probability) is arguably more judiciously
determined. It certainly would be more time costly, but the threshold I
suspect be strongly more rigorous against false positive inclusions.

In any case, if you want to get at those terms in eq 11/12, here's what I
recommend:
1. See the method in [[https://github.com/jlizier/jidt/blob/master/java/source/infodynamics/measures/continuous/kraskov/ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov1.java][ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov1]]
   (line 68). By line 197 you have the counts n_{yz}(i), n_{xz}(i) and
   n_z(i) for point i. K (indeed digamma(K) is already stored as a constant
   there).
2. You can easily compute digamma(N) since N is stored as the variable
   totalObservations
3. You then just need n_x(i), or n_y(i), depending on which way around
   you're doing it. To compute that, you would need to:
  a. Construct a new object nnSearcherX (say, for n_x) in the super class
     [[https://github.com/jlizier/jidt/blob/master/java/source/infodynamics/measures/continuous/kraskov/ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov.java][ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov]] (near line 491)
     mirroring  the creation of nnSearcherConditional for the conditional
     variable z, but there obviously for x or y (being var1Observations or
     var2Observations, depending on which way around you go).
  b. Coming back to [[https://github.com/jlizier/jidt/blob/master/java/source/infodynamics/measures/continuous/kraskov/ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov1.java][ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov1]] you
     then need to add a call on that nnSearcherX object (say after
     line 189) to get n_x as
     nnSearcherX.countPointsWithinR(t,kthNnData.distance, dynCorrExclTime, false).
4. Finally, you need to put all these counts together now in your eqs 11
   and 12 around that line 197 to compute the two quantities you
   want. That's the tricky part. I'd suggest hijacking the results[] array
   around line 239. Then you hack the way the components of that array are
   used back in [[https://github.com/jlizier/jidt/blob/master/java/source/infodynamics/measures/continuous/kraskov/ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov.java][ConditionalMutualInfoCalculatorMultiVariateKraskov]] (after
   line 554). Obviously instead of returning one number (conditional MI)
   you'd need to return an array with two numbers (the two MIs).

Hope that helps,
--joe
+61 408 186 901 (Au mobile)

***** <<Feature selection for probabilistic forecasts>>

      Most (all?) feature selection papers are about feature selection for
      point regression or classification.  Here are papers about feature
      selection that improves not only point forecast error, but measures of
      error distribution error
      e.g. [[Continuous Ranked Probability Score (CRPS)]]

******* The [[http://support.sas.com/documentation/cdl/en/statug/63962/HTML/default/viewer.htm#statug_qreg_sect016.htm][QUANTREG Procedure]]
        QR can have different or the same dependences between the inputs and
        the output quantiles.  So can have a more complex, switching model or
        a sparse one.

        From their manual:

          In quantile regression analysis, you might be interested in testing
          whether a covariate effect is statistically signficant for a given
          quantile. In other situations, you might be interested in testing
          whether the coeficients of a covariate are the same across a set of
          quantiles. You can use the TEST Statement to perform these tests.

***** Bunches improves stability, so no momentum filter?
******* but it's faster

*** Recommends 5-fold CV for penalized spline QR: [[file:energy.bib::Reiss12smthPenSplnQR][Reiss & Huang 2012: Smoothness]]

***** Gaussian Process [[http://mlg.eng.cam.ac.uk/duvenaud/cookbook/index.html][periodic kernel]]
*** Angular in input (e.g. wind direction)
    <<Angular In Input>>
***** why [spd*sin(dir), spd*cos(dir)] isn't good enough
      <<why not sin/cos?>>
      i.e. velocity basis must be more complex than sin(dir)/cos(dir)
******* only limited spd/dir relationships expressable by 2 linear coeffs

        Effect of wind velocity on a linear regression

          a1 * spd * cos(dir)
          a2 * spd * sin(dir)

        where a1,a2 are learned regression coeffs.  This can't learn a
        realistic dir vs. effect function because:

        1. Can't represent unequal effects for N. vs S or E. vs W.
        2. Can't rotate: Effect parallel to only X or Y axes: oblong X or Y only

        - *Example*:

        source('~/lib/R/sutil.R')
        library(R.utils)

        dir=seq(0,2*pi,0.1)
        spd=1.0
        A = vvcombo(1:3,1:3)
        lims = sqrt(max(A[,1] * A[,2])) * c(-1,1)

        subplots(nrow=3, ncol=3)
        for(i in 1:nrow(A)) {
          plot(A[i,1]*cos(dir),A[i,2]*sin(dir),xlim=lims,ylim=lims,main=paste('A:',A[i,1],A[i,2]),asp=1,pty='s')
        }
******* cos(dir) and sin(dir) inputs can only do additive power/dir relationship

        This is wrong for wind power because when there is
        zero wind speed, a directional term should only add zero but you
        can't express that with an additive term.  Need at least a
        [[Varying%20coefficient%20models][Varying coefficient models]] or a periodic basis.

******* [[Periodic splines]] are better than sin/cos: [[file:energy.bib::Kaufman05perSplnRgrsn][Kaufman et al. 2005: Spline]]
        (has R and Matlab)
******* [[file:energy.bib::Boydstun80comp3DmaxReach][Boydstun et al. 1980]] explains well how to build periodic spline basis
******* only need cos(dir) for angular kernel: [[file:energy.bib::Kaufman05perSplnRgrsn][Kaufman et al. 2005: Spline]]
******* k=2 Fourier coeffs is enough (he does sin/cos): [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]]
******* see also: [[Physics-based power curve features]]
******* see [[Harmonic Periodic Bases]]
***** see also [[Circular Statistics]]
***** [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]] does this with Fourier [[Interaction terms]]

*********** max correlation / mutual info with regression output
************* for only this lagged velocity meas?
************* something like?  [[file:energy.bib::Mann11smoothDerivInfo][Mann et al. 2011: Using]] (info to smooth derivative)
*********** Nice tutorials on linear interactions: [[http://www.r-bloggers.com/r-tutorial-series-regression-with-interaction-variables/][here]] and [[http://math.uprm.edu/~wrolke/esma3102/discretepredict.htm][here]], and [[http://rtutorialseries.blogspot.com/2010/01/r-tutorial-series-basic-hierarchical.html][selecting them with ANOVA]].

************* and others

******* direction via circular harmonics
********* could project wind speed onto [[http://www.blackpawn.com/texts/ch/default.html][circular harmonics]] of direction
********* takes advantage of DFT periodic extension
********* but need N sin/cos pairs to represent /function/ of spd/dir @ N spatial freqs
********* bases are orthogonal (great for having uncorrelated inputs)
********* can do asymmetric shapes w/ continuity @ 0/360 degree wraparound
********* # of harmonics depends upon desired reconstruction accuracy
*********** of "true" spd vs. dir (I guess this will be the mean relationship here)
*********** harmonic bases can interpolate between, and don't need all N?
********* Is this more or less efficent/orthogonal than periodic splines?

******* Spherical harmonics worse than spline when have non-uniform sampling?
        <<spherical harmonics worse than spline?>>
        [[http://www.lpi.usra.edu/meetings/lpsc2008/pdf/2338.pdf][- Spherical Splines: Beyond Spherical Harmonics for Non-Uniform Geophysical Datasets on the Moon and Mercury]]
        - could circular (2D sphere) have same problem?
        - The reason given is the "global support" required for spherical
        - makes sense: harmonic spreads across entire spatial extent,
          but would only want a bump (say) in the response in one area
        - But maybe not so important if only 2D? (space is less sparse)
        - [[file:energy.bib::Boydstun80comp3DmaxReach][Boydstun et al. 1980]] (reach is more spherical?)

********* [[file:energy.bib::Boydstun80comp3DmaxReach][Boydstun et al. 1980]]: spherical spline (but sph. harm. maybe better
********* Periodic knots
          <<Periodic knots>>

          For normal spline, you repeat boundary knots to clamp the edge
          values.  For periodic splines, instead of repeating, you wrap
          around to the beginning (or the end) and copy the opposite edge
          knots, kind of like circular convolution in DFT's or wavelets.

          See also: [[Spline knot choice]]

          Kind of explains it: [[file:energy.bib::Eilers10SplnsKntsPnlties][Eilers & Marx 2010: Splines]]

*********** [[file:energy.bib::Boydstun80comp3DmaxReach][Boydstun et al. 1980]] is clear about periodic spline construction
            esp. at the repeating boundary knots
*********** [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/pbs/index.html][R package pbs]]: easily portable code for periodic b-splines basis
*********** [[http://www.pigei.com/computer-vision/5-bspline][Matlab showing periodic knot construction]], also uses Matlab spline toolbox (spmak())
********* [[http://stat.ethz.ch/R-manual/R-devel/library/splines/html/periodicSpline.html][periodicSpline{spline}]] (periodic, not lagged)
********* Periodic splines are better than Fourier-like bases: [[file:energy.bib::Kaufman05perSplnRgrsn][Kaufman et al. 2005: Spline]]
          and only need cos term in fourier kernel expansion
********* Penalized, periodic splines [[file:energy.bib::Eilers10SplnsKntsPnlties][Eilers & Marx 2010: Splines]]
********* R [[http://ugrad.stat.ubc.ca/R/library/fda/html/create.bspline.basis.html][create.bspline.bassis{fda}]] says Fourier bases are better for periodic splines

          But how penalize or smooth them?  [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]] doesn't
          even try.

    (a kind of whitening)

***** in Matlab
******* Matlab's built-in [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/signal/index.html%3F/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/signal/lpc.html&http://www.google.com/search%3Fq%3Dinverse%2Blinear%2Bprediction%2Bmatlab&ie%3Dutf-8&oe%3Dutf-8&aq%3Dt&rls%3Dorg.mozilla:en-US:official&client%3Dfirefox-a][lpc.m]]
******* voicebox [[http://www.ee.ic.ac.uk/hp/staff/dmb/voicebox/lpc.html][lpc functions]]
***** speech tools, as in my thesis

      # do inverse filter
      $step->cmd("$speech_tools_dir/sig2fv -lpc_order <ifilt_nLPC opt> "
      . " -coefs lpc -otype est"
      ." -shift <ifilt_frmShiftT opt> -preemph <ifilt_preemph opt>"
      ." $bpfOutVar -o <lpcoefs tmp>"); # get coeffs

      $xcInVar[$pI]="<xcinput_$pI tmp>";
      $step->cmd("$speech_tools_dir/sigfilter -inv_filter "
      . " -lpcfilter <lpcoefs tmp> $bpfOutVar"
      . " -o $xcInVar[$pI]"); # filter it

* <<Causality determination>>
*** Markov Blanket MI approach to feat sel: [[file:energy.bib::Herrera06effectInputSelFuncApprox][Herrera et al. 2006: Effective Input Variable]]
*** perhaps a better MB learner:  [[file:energy.bib::Pellet08markovBlankCausLrn][Pellet & Elisseeff 2008: Using Markov Blankets]]
***** uses (and defines) [[partial correlation]] for causal det. (better ways?)
*** video lecture: [[http://videolectures.net/ida07_pellet_apcba/][A Partial Correlation-Based Algorithm for Causal Structure Discovery with Continuous Variables]]
***** [[partial coherence]] can catch time dependence
***** so can [[Partial Mutual Information Estimation]]
***** mutual information detects nonlin relationships, maybe too hard for giant-dim graphs in 1st step of this approach
*** [[http://www.clopinet.com/isabelle/Projects/NIPS2008/slides/Tillman_nips08_causality_slides.pdf][When causality matters for prediction:Investigating the practical tradeoffs]]
***** From: [[http://www.clopinet.com/isabelle/Projects/NIPS2008/][NIPS 2008 Workshop on Causality]] (several good papers and slides)
***** [[http://videolectures.net/coa08_tillman_wcmfp/][video lecture]]
***** Conclusion:

      If accidentally train on children of thing to be predicted and the
      children are noisy during test, then there will be a problem.

      _But_ errors in causality determination (which may be parametric) may
      be bad enough that simpler, non-parametric non-causal methods may
      work better.  Note: I think they said they were working w/ 1000
      variables in the video.

      _My comment_: they used linear causality techniques (I think) and
      compared against SVM's (I think, better check).  Also, I think
      everything in these studies were instantaneous so no time lag
      clues.  Finally, there is the noise coherence way of detecting
      causality.

on sat, oct 22, 2011 at 2:19 pm, sera choma <sera.onalan@gmail.com> wrote:

hi,

i would like to set bounds for some of my variables. for example i have a
variable that measures the number of health personnel in a given province.
the min should be 0, but i do not require a max bound. what would be the
best approach for this type of bound? should i be setting the max to
infinity?

also, i have set a bound for one of my dependent variables that is a
percentage of votes in a given province. the min is 0 and the max is 1.
however, when i impute my data the min for this variable is -1.388e-17,
which is nearly 0. i am not sure why this happens and if it is ok for me to
keep a negative number (even though it is so small) as my dependent variable
(that is a proportion). any suggestions?

thank you for your help.

sera
***** arcsin(sqrt(x/powMax)): [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes04windLocQR][Bremnes 2004: Probabilistic]]
***** logit "logistic" xform, asin or probit are possibilties: [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes06compQuantileWind][Bremnes 2006]]: probabilistic comparison

      Calls it the "logistic" function but transform is  [[https://personality-project.org/r/psych/help/logistic.html][really a
      logit()]]; the untransform _after_ regression is logistic.

***** logit SDE xform: [[file:energy.bib::Moller13windFrcstSDE][Moeller et al. 2013: Probabilistic Forecasts Wind]]
***** [[Beta regression]]
***** [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kumaraswamy_distribution][Kumaraswamy Distribution]]
***** ensure non-negative w/ log (Matlab ksdensity)

      for example, see the [[http://www.mathworks.de/help/toolbox/stats/ksdensity.html][help]] for the matlab ksdensity function:

      if the support parameter is 'positive', ksdensity transforms x
      using a log function, estimates the density of the transformed
      values, and transforms back to the original scale. if support is a
      vector [l u], ksdensity uses the transformation
      log((x-l)/(u-x)). the width parameter and u outputs are on the
      scale of the transformed values.

        that it doesn't change w/ the mean (I think).

* <<Time delay estimation>>
*** use for turbine interrelationship clustering
*** another explanation for why lags might make sense: [[file:energy.bib::Lu07lagEnsemble][Lu et al. 2007: Short Range Numerical]]
*** Max/Min lag? ie. how fast do wind speed changes move across space?
***** Big feat dim reduction if only check within turb-interdist-dep. lag range
***** [[file:energy.bib::BPA07inHourBalanceRqt][BPA: In Hour Balancing]] has BPA inter-farm lags
***** a guess: 3.5-10 m/s
*** regression with lagged copies of inputs
***** [[Dynamic PCA]] does this
***** problem: multicolinearity

      Lagged versions of variable are so highly correlated with each
      other that their coefficients can be estimated only very
      imprecisely ([[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_lag][Wikipedia]]: Distributed lag)

      My take: There are a lot of parameters to estimate in a tricky,
      colinear situation.  Needs lots of data or get non-generalizable
      results.

      Some hints on what to do about colinearity: [[file:energy.bib::Friendly12CollinRgrssn][Friendly 2012: Collinearity]]

***** Solution? [[Distributed lag]]
***** Solution? partial correlation?
*** <<Distributed lag>>: force structure on lags and then estimate them

    *Overview*: smoothness-constrained lag profile allows normal linear
    regression w/o copying a ton of lagged variables.  Therefore, fewer
    coeffs in model. There are many types but the two most important seem
    to be polynomial and spline, which can be estimated with ordinary
    least squares regression techniques (maybe even w/ shrinkage or
    whatever).  Spline seems to be the latest and greatest, since it is
    more flexible yet better behaved than poly.

***** Distributed Lag Basis with constrained "latest input" fit

      *Overview*: In forecasting, the most recent input is almost always
      the best, and therefore, it's a good idea to make sure it's
      reproduced exactly, even it it's expressed in a distributed lag
      basis function.

      For polynomials, this is simple.  Consider a 2nd order poly:

         y = a*x^2 + b*x + c

      Here, y is the distributed lag basis value for different lags, x.
      For the most recent lag, x=0, so:

        y = x*0 + b*0 + c

        ==> y = c

        ==> y = a*x^2 + b*x + y0

      Where y0 is the latest measurement; where a and b are solved for
      using lags of y; and where x is scaled to model N discretely
      lagged input samples:

        x = 1/N;  N>=2

      For a polynomial of order p, the reduction in inputs to the
      regression model that takes the lagged basis coefficients as input
      is then:

        fracNumInputs = p/(N+1);

      e.g. for a 15 minute sample period; a 2 hour max lag; and a 2nd
      order poly, the reduction in inputs is:

        frac15s_2hr = 2 / (2*4 + 1) = 2/9 = 0.22

      _Colinearity_: Polynomial lag bases are said to cause collinearity
      problems ([[file:energy.bib::McDowell04polyDistLag][McDowell 2004: From]]), blowing up linear regression, and I
      think NN's, LASSO, and other algorithms.  But doesn't this problem
      go away if you just do PCA/PLS/sufficient/Fourier/wavelet/Chebyshev/ICA
      or some other orthogonal transform?  This could also actually make
      /make collinearity a benefit/ because that would allow additional
      dimension reduction.  But, hints about what to do about
      colinearity: [[file:energy.bib::Friendly12CollinRgrssn][Friendly 2012: Collinearity]]

      TODO: train some of these things to see what polynomial shapes are
      produced.  Also, consider using tensor splines with interaction
      terms (I saw paper, I think, which made a basis function out of
      these)

***** The [[http://support.sas.com/documentation/cdl/en/statug/63962/HTML/default/viewer.htm#statug_qreg_sect016.htm][QUANTREG Procedure]]

      QR can have different or the same dependences between the inputs and
      the output quantiles.  So can have a more complex, switching model or
      a sparse one.

      From their manual:

        In quantile regression analysis, you might be interested in testing
        whether a covariate effect is statistically signficant for a given
        quantile. In other situations, you might be interested in testing
        whether the coeficients of a covariate are the same across a set of
        quantiles. You can use the TEST Statement to perform these tests.

***** Quantile regression and ABC
      <<Quantile regression and ABC>>
      Improve QR high dim probs w/ ABC?
******* [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximate_Bayesian_computation][Approximate Bayesian Computation]] (ABC)

        - General monte-carlo-type way of doing any Bayesian thing, I think
        - But more efficient than plain monte carlo:
           - instead of the usual distribution estimation, works on summary
             statistics, like mean, variance
           - and maybe quantiles?
           - paper below (R package) has trick to make it more efficient
        - good for high dimensions
        - could use this for spinning reserve optimization, also, mabye
        - optimal bidding (given forecast distribution)
        - better/adaptive forecasting? (see [[Adaptive Training / Updating]])

        - *R package* has non-linear correction making ABC much more efficient
          [[file:energy.bib::Blum10nonlinApproxBayesComp][Blum & Francois 2010: Non Approximate Bayesian Computation]]

*********** [[file:energy.bib::Liu09crvRegisClustFunc][Liu & Yang 2009: Simultaneous]]  (curv reg. and func dat clustering)

***** Multiple output quantile regresson
      <<Multiple output quantile regresson>>

      Good for:
       - multiple horizon quantiles e.g. for markets?
       - scenarios (given input, sample the quantile dist to get scenario)
       - joint solar/wind?
       - wind speed AND dir? Or U and V
       - outlier detection

*********** constraints for roughness, mono, etc.
******* [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/answers/93062-is-there-a-routine-to-perform-quantile-regression-or-lad-least-absolute-deviations-in-matlab][Recommends fminunc()]] in Matlab optimization toolbox, or robustfit() (stats toolbox)

        but fminunc() is unconstrained optimization; you'd want a
        constrained interior point algorithm, right?

******* Matlab's [[http://www.mathworks.com/products/optimization/features.html][constrained interior point]] algorithms
********* [[http://www.mathworks.com/help/optim/ug/constrained-nonlinear-optimization-algorithms.html][introduction]]
********* [[http://www.mathworks.com/help/optim/ug/fmincon-interior-point-algorithm-with-analytic-hessian.html][fmincon()]]: with or without a Hessian (faster with)
********* Hessian could come from [[*Complex%20Step%20Derivative%20(CSD)%20Approximation][Complex Step Derivative (CSD) Approximation]]?
******* [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/fileexchange/32115-quantreg-x-y-tau-order-nboot-][quantreg.m]] Matlab Central function.

        Does an unconstrained optimization of the quantile loss function.
        Seems like it would be buggy.

        Says it requires Optimization and Stats toolboxes, but it only uses
        fminsearch() which is standard.

******* Matlab [[http://www.econ.uiuc.edu/~roger/research/rq/rq.m][code for interior point method]]

        From [[http://www.econ.uiuc.edu/~roger/research/rq/rq.html][here]]:

        A basic version of the interior point (Frisch-Newton) algorithm for
        quantile regression developed for the R quantreg package is also
        available for matlab. A C++ translation of the algorithm is also
        available from Ron Gallant's libcpp library. This algorithm is
        described in Koenker and Portnoy (Statistical Science, 1997).

******* [[http://sites.stat.psu.edu/~dhunter/code/qrmatlab/][Dhunter Generic QR Matlab Code]] (linear, polynomial,...) (Dhunter of PSU)
        <<Dhunter Generic QR Matlab Code>>

        you input a handle to a regression function and its derivative, and
        dhunter's code estimates the regression parameters.

        could be an easy way to do spline basis.  not sure about local
        linear, seems like you still have to put a loop around that.

        ipqr.m is interior point algorithm: [[file:energy.bib::koenker96intptqr][koenker & park 1996]] interior qr

******* polynomial qr ([[http://www.mathworks.de/matlabcentral/fileexchange/32115-quantreg-m-quantile-regression][quantreg.m]] from matlab central)

******* [[http://homepages.ulb.ac.be/~dpaindav/research/code.html][multiple-output regression quantile regions]] (good multiple horizon qunatiles? joint solar/wind?)
******* [[http://web.missouri.edu/~kaplandm/code/ivqr_see.m][ivqr_see.m]] smoothed instrumental variable qr.  i didn't quite understand

*** <<Distribution to Distribution Regression>>

    Predict a distribution conditional on some other distribution.  The
    input and output distributions don't have to have the same number of
    samples.  Useful, for example, when you get many samples in one time
    frame and want to predict the distribution of the samples in the next
    time frame.

    Potential uses: 1) ensemble calibration (inputs are ensemble wind
                       speeds, outputs are ensemble wind powers
                       - would only make sense for single farm since speeds
                         don't add
                       - would be a kind of [[Power Curve Learning]]
                    2) quantile persistence forecast, as in [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]] or [[cite:Dokic15systIntegLrgData][Dokic et al. 2015: Systematic Integration Large (prob. persist & more)]]
                       - similar to Markov time-dependence for prob forecast
                    3.) could be used for analog ensembles (forecast from
                        past distributions)

***** [[file:energy.bib::Oliva13dist2distRgrssn][Oliva et al. 2013: Distribution]] to dist rgrssn: must for market prices?
***** [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]] (a kind of quantile persistence, but not as fancy)
***** [[cite:Dokic15systIntegLrgData][Dokic et al. 2015: Systematic Integration Large (prob. persist & more)]]

***** Bootstrap vs. cross-validation
      <<Bootstrap vs. cross-validation>>

      Opinion seems to be that CV (low bias, high variance) is for model
      selection and measurement of predictive accuracy while BS is for
      measuring output uncertainty (high (pessimistic) bias, low
      uncertainty), once you have a model. (but [[file:energy.bib::Harrell15rgrssnMdlStrtgyBook][Harrell 2015: Regression]]
      thinks BS requires fewer samples)

      Also BS is good when have little data, although bias is worse then
      when it's used on large datasets.

      Also, it seems to me that CV is better when have non-IID data
      e.g. forecasts w/ temporal dependence.

      Leave-one-out cross-validation is unloved b/c the variance isn't reduced.

******* commenter has [[http://stats.stackexchange.com/questions/18348/differences-between-cross-validation-and-bootstrapping-to-estimate-the-predictio][nice summary]] w/ many refs, likes repeated CV, but some don't elsewhere)
******* neual FAQ: [[ftp://ftp.sas.com/pub/neural/FAQ3.html#A_cross][What are cross-validation and bootstrapping? ]]
******* see also: [[Train/test partitioning schemes]]

***** My Lame Thinking
******* <<Copulas in Matlab>>
        From: [[https://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/newsreader/view_thread/51600][MATLAB Central - matlabcode for copulas]]

        _Basic Gaussian Idea_
        1: Generate /normal multivariate random/ w/ desired linear covariance (rho)
           z: an MVN w/ desired linear correlation structure

        2: Convert MVN numbers, z, to uniform
           u = invGaussianCdf(z):

        3: Convert uniform numbers to the final marginal distributions, x

           x(:,1) = gaminv(u(:,1)) ; dim 1 has gamma distribution
           x(:,2) = gaminv(u(:,2)) ; dim 2 has t distribution


        _Basic Student t distribution idea_

        1: Generate /t multivariate random/ w/ desired linear covariance (rho)

        2: Convert T distributed data to uniform
           u = invTcdf(z):

        3: same as for Gaussian

        _Example Code_

        % Gaussian Copula
        n = 500;
        tau = .8; % specify the rank correlation
        rho = 2*asin(tau)/pi; % get the required linear correlation for the MVN
        z = mvnrnd([0 0], [1 rho; rho 1], n);
        u = normcdf(z); % correlated uniforms
        x = [gaminv(u(:,1),2,1) tinv(u(:,2),5)];

        % Students T copula
        n = 500;
        tau = .8; % specify the rank correlation
        rho = 2*asin(tau)/pi; % get the required linear correlation for the MVT
        nu = 1;
        z = mvtrnd([1 rho; rho 1], nu, n);
        u = tcdf(z,nu); % correlated uniforms
        x = [gaminv(u(:,1),2,1) tinv(u(:,2),5)];

        See [[T-Distribution]]

******* Linear correlation in original space not preserved; rank correlations are
        From: [[https://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/newsreader/view_thread/314203][MATLAB Central - Copulas to simulate gaussian and binary data.]]

        /Peter Perkins says/:

        Linear correlation is something you pretty much have to give up on with copulas. It just _isn't preserved_ under nonlinear transformations like inverse CDFs. Sometimes you _can choose the copula parameters to get the right linear correlation_ on the marginals, but then if you change the marginals by something _other than a scale/shift, you lose the_ desired linear correlation. What's worse, there are simple examples out there (google this) that demonstrate that for some marginals, some linear correlation values are _not achievable_ at all.

        So I think most people think instead about rank correlations, which are preserved under inverse CDF transformations. The _CORR function will happily compute either Spearman's or Kendall's_ rank correlation, and the _COPULAPARAM function will give you the copula parameter (your rho)_ to get the desired rank correlation.

        So, [[https://www.mathworks.com/help/stats/copulaparam.html][COPULAPARAM]], given a Spearman/Kendall corr. gives you the Normal or "t" copula linear correlation.

********* [[http://www.psychstat.missouristate.edu/multibook/mlt08.htm][effect of correlated variables on linear regression]]

*correlated and uncorrelated predictor variables*

adding variables to a linear regression model will always increase the
unadjusted r2 value. if the additional predictor variables are correlated
with the predictor variables already in the model, then the combined
results are difficult to predict. in some cases, the combined result will
provide only a slightly better prediction, while in other cases, a much
better prediction than expected will be the outcome of combining two
correlated variables.

if the additional predictor variables are uncorrelated (r = 0) with the
predictor variables already in the model, then the result of adding
additional variables to the regression model is easy to predict. namely the
r2 change will be equal to the correlation coefficient squared between the
added variable and predicted variable. in this case it makes no difference
what order the predictor variables are entered into the prediction
model. for example, if x1 and x2 were uncorrelated (r12 = 0) and r1y2 = .3
and r2y2 = .4, then r2 for x1 and x2 would equal .3 + .4 = .7. the value
for r2 change for x2 given x1 was in the model would be .4. the value for
r2 change for x2 given no variable was in the model would be .4. it would
make no difference at what stage x2 was entered into the model, the value
for r2 change would always be .4. similarly, the r2 change value for x1
would always be .3. because of this relationship, uncorrelated predictor
variables will be preferred, when possible.

***** kalman filter approaches with multiple models

      idea is to gradually learn different regimes by multiple
      hypothesis target tracking (mht).  this is probably nonlinear,
      must deal with "occlusion" when the regime isn't active, (and
      probably must have a variable dimensional state model, for missing
      data?).

******* [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/stamp/stamp.jsp?tp%3d&arnumber%3d1683370&usertype%3dinst&tag%3d1][propagation parameter tracking using variable state dimension kalman filter]]

***** _oracle experiment_: showing that regime switching would help

      let cp-var, power curve learner, or whatever, run adaptively as
      usual, storing learned coeffs @ each step.  re-run each stored
      coeff set over the entire data record.  foreach time, pick coeff
      set that got best forecasting result.  if see that best coeffs were
      seen before the time they were best, then could have conceivably
      stored them as a "regime" and could have applied them without
      waiting for adaptation.

      how much better would performance have been with this perfect
      regime detection?

********* seems like does partial correlation: explanation of [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/addedvarplot.html][addedvarplot.m]]:

          added variable plots are used to determine the unique effect of
          adding a new term to a multilinear model. the plot shows the
          _relationship between the part of the response unexplained by terms_
          _already in the model and the part of the new term unexplained by_
          _terms already in the model_. the "unexplained" parts are measured by
          the residuals of the respective regressions. a scatter of the
          residuals from the two regressions forms the added variable plot.

********* ignores entire row if any element is missing
******* [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/mvregress.html][mvregress.m]] fills in missing values?, based on *algorithm* param, somehow

        *algorithm* — either 'ecm' to compute the maximum likelihood
        estimates via the ecm algorithm, 'cwls' to perform least squares
        (optionally conditionally weighted by an input covariance matrix), or
        'mvn' to omit observations with missing features and compute the ordinary
        multivariate normal estimates. the *default* is _mvn' for complete_
        data, _ecm' for missing features when the sample size is sufficient_ to
        estimate all parameters, and _cwls' otherwise_.

        *however*: matlab support says ignores entire row if any element is missing:

        *anyway* gets exactly the same answer as final stepwisefit.m, when
        given stepwisefit.m's inmodel vector

******* [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/mvregresslike.html][mvregresslike.m]] does neg log likelihood regression, use w/ bic?
******* [[http://www.mathworks.com/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/index.html%3f/access/helpdesk/help/toolbox/stats/robustfit.html&http://www.mathworks.com/cgi-bin/texis/webinator/search/%3fdb%3dmss&prox%3dpage&rorder%3d750&rprox%3d750&rdfreq%3d500&rwfreq%3d500&rlead%3d250&sufs%3d0&order%3dr&is_summary_on%3d1&resultcount%3d10&query%3drobust%2bregression&submitbuttonname%3dsearch][robustfit.m]] supposed to be more robust to outliers

      - [[lasso feature selection]]
        - handles dim>nsamps
        - supposed to be fast
        - stable (s/ help w/ regime clustering)
        - ties to bma
        - matlab available
        - has time series extensions
        - can be adaptive
        - trick to parallelize giant dims across multiple machines
        - but is still linear...  i think lasso video said ok as nonlinear preproc
        - implement cross-validation, as in [[file:energy.bib::tibshirani96lasso][tibshirani 1996: regression]]
          - why people pick 10-fold cross-validation: [[file:energy.bib::refaeilzadeh09crossval][liu & oezsu 2009: encyclopedia]] cross-validation
        - decide on linearization
          what inputs or output to log to make it more linear, matching
          lasso model

***** nwp for short term forecasts [0/3]
      - [ ] nwp confidence metric
            - see [[file:energy.bib::geyer06subsampbootstrap][geyer 2006: notes]] (subsampling bootstrap)
      - [ ] separate feature selection for nwp vars?

            - needed to learn nonlinear confidence metrics
            - combine w/ power prediction too?  use what's learned by
              training pow curve?
      - [ ] use my prosody quicknet input confidence mlp [/]
        - [ ] get permission frm mari
      - [ ] nwp spatio/temporal front lookahead:

            assumption is that temporal correlation/mi _across space_ right now
            gives you more confidence in the nwp forecast than just
            correlation/mi of nwp with data _only at the plant_ right now.
            hopefully, this helps w/ ramp forecasting.

        - vs. offiste obs
          - look at locations and lags selected by offsite obs feature selection
          - is nwp correlating well w/ the obs there right now?
          - if so, then maybe the nwp forecast for the obs location will also
            be right ie. can estimate the future obs (plug this in somehow?)
          - if so, then is nwp forecast good @ the site?

        - vs. old nwp runs
          - do virtual observation feature selection with real plant spd/pow
            - ie use nwp data in place of real observations
            - and do "offsite obs" selection
          - somehow, use this dependency to determine if nwp is working

***** correlation (subspace) clustering
      <<correlation clustering>>
******* good [[http://www.dbs.ifi.lmu.de/cms/clustering_high-dimensional_data][overview]]
******* finds points that are on the same line/plane/hyperspace
******* being on line means you can build a predictive relationship
******* seems to be good for high dims
******* relation to other correlation based linear methods?

******* some can find arbitrary orientations with mixed dimensions and overlaps
******* and [[http://edoc.ub.uni-muenchen.de/8736/1/zimek_arthur.pdf][thesis]], esp. w/ hierarchical, arbitrary, varying sdims
******* refs 1-6 in paper points to some good ones:
        "a general framework for increasing the robustness of pca-based correlation clustering algorithms"
        _tangent_: [[http://bm2.genes.nig.ac.jp/rgm2/r_current/library/corpcor/man/mvr.shrink.html][mvr.shrink {corpcor}]]:can weight each data point (but not dimension, apparently)
******* mixed dims is a kind of feature selection
********* [[http://www.dbs.ifi.lmu.de/cms/clustering_high-dimensional_data][axis-projected or parallel]] algorithms would do hard feature selection

***** autocorrelation-weighted persistence as a metric:

        this was in somebody's paper:

        a = rxx(tlookahead)/rxx(0)

        forecast = a * persistence + (1-a) * climatology

        might want to remove diurnal comps too.

*** Basic Forecasting Techniques
***** Holt Winters: simple, robust, & better know
******* nice review: [[File:energy.bib::meyer02naivefrcstmethr][Meyer 2002: Naive time series forecasting methods]]

        really simple, and i guess, robust. there's just one coefficient to
        estimate for each additional trick:

        o exponential weighting
        o trend
        o seasonal
        o multipliciative seasonal

        These are R built-in functions, do est. by least squares.  Confidence
        bounds included.  These are mostly Holt Winters techniques.
******* Holt exp linear: separate trend, bias smoothing: [[file:energy.bib::Nau15smoothMAexpHolt][Nau 2015: Moving]] avg exp smth
******* additive or multipicatative seasonal: [[file:energy.bib::UKONS08holtWintersARIMAreg][National 2008: From Holt Winters ARIMA Modelling]]
******* multi-periodicity (daily, weekly): [[file:energy.bib::Szmit12holtWinterMultiPeriod][Szmit & Szmit 2012: Usage Holt Winters]]
******* additive periodicity, conf. int., transforms: [[file:energy.bib::Bermudez07holtWintersAddPer][Bermudez et al. 2007: Holt]]
******* exponential weighting (simple HW) for quantiles: [[file:energy.bib::Taylor07frcstSprMktPriceQR][Taylor 2007: Forecasting]]
******* trend damping is better, almost regime learn: [[file:energy.bib::McKenzie10expSmthDampTrnd][McKenzie & Gardner 2010: Damped]] trend
******* primary paper? [[file:energy.bib::Winters60exponMvAvgSalesFrcst][Winters 1960: Forecasting]]
***** ARIMA, etc.
******* [[file:energy.bib::UKONS08holtWintersARIMAreg][National 2008: From Holt Winters ARIMA Modelling]] : trend + multip/add seasonal
***** Caltech video: [[http://itunes.apple.com/us/podcast/where-wind-comes-from-on-earth/id422627541?i%3d91602098][where the wind comes from]]

*** <<Aggregation vs. Forecasting Accuracy>>
***** aggregate is smoother and easier to forecast
******* [[File:energy.bib::siebert08regpowforecast][Siebert 2008: development of methods]]
******* [[File:energy.bib::giebel07erraggregwindpow][Giebel et al. 2007: forecast error of]]
******* [[File:energy.bib::wu07litrevwindforecast][Wu & hong 2007: literature review of]]
******* [[File:energy.bib::ahlstrom05futurewindforecastutil][Ahlstrom et al. 2005]]
***** aggregate requires fewer measurements (from wind farms)
***** but somewhat harder to handle individual outages
******* more important for short time scales

***** hierarchical forecast make be best?  [[file:energy.bib::athanasopoulos09hierfrcst][athanasopoulos et al. 2009: hierarchical australian]]
***** can aggegation be a submodulal problem?
******* e.g. characterizing a gaussian spatial field w/ min. observations
********* see ph measurement location selection example [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/fileexchange/20504-submodular-function-optimization/content/sfo/html/sfo_tutorial_pub.html][here]]

***** <<Converting Product to Sums>>

      Many relationships e.g. direction and wind speed in power curves
      are products, making linear regression hard, because it is a
      weighted sum.  How to convert products to sums?

      _I got several hits when I googled this but lost all but the one below_

******* email to Ole Chrisensen

Hello Dr. Christensen,

Scott Otterson, here, a DTU-IMM post-doc working with Henrik Madsen on wind
power forecasting.  Do you have time to give me some advice?

I'm predicting wind power production from a set of geographically
distributed wind velocity measurements.  I'm starting with linear
prediction because of the large catalog of linear techniques for subspace
tracking, adaptation, and predictor selection.  But since the dependence
structure is far from linear, I would like to develop basis functions that
make it more so.

Specifically, I'm looking for a compact basis function for lagged,
nonlineary warped wind velocity.

SOME DETAILS

I would like to learn the function, L():

  o(t) = L(m(t,1), m(t,2),... m(t,N)) + e(t)

where o(t) is the power to be predicted, e(t) is the error, and m(t,n) is
the vector of lagged wind velocity measurements for site n:

  m(t,n) = [s(t,n),d(t,n),s(t-1,n),d(t-1,n),... d(t-K,n))];   n=1..N;

where s(t,n) and d(t,n) are speed and direction measurements; and where
K is some maximum lag.

Because the number of potential lags, K, is large, and because direction
has a nonlinear effect on the relationship between power and speed, I would
like to nonlinearly project m(t,n) onto a small vector of basis
coefficients, v(t,n), which has an approximately linear relationship with
p(t):

  p(t) "varies linearly with" Lv(v(t,1),v(t,2),... v(t,N))

where Lv() a projection function.


TENSOR PRODUCT OF MARGINALS

A simple approach would be to start with a linear function of the
marginals.  For example, I could build a lagged speed vector, S(t):

  S(t) = [s(t,1),s(t-1,1),... s(t-K,1),s(t,2),... s(t-K,N)]

and then use LASSO, LARS, [[Covariance Shrinkage]], etc., to select signficant
measurement sites and lags (assume, for the moment, that s(t,n) is somehow
warped so that the relation between wind speed and power is linear).  Two
immediate problems are that the elements of S(t), are highly correlated,
making the linear regression covariance matrix estimation unstable, and
that the dimension of S(t) may be large compared to the number of
measurements available during a short period of temporal stationarity
during which a regression function estimation must be made.

An improvement would be to compress

   Sn(t,n)=[s(t,n), s(t-1,n),... s(t-k,n)]

by projecting lagged speed onto a basis function running in the lag
direction.  For example, I could require that Sn's contribution to the
prediction, Snl, be a linear function of lagged speeds:

   Snl(t,n) = dot_product(Sn(t,n),beta(n))

where beta is a vector of coefficients whose values are a polynomial in
lag:

   beta(n) = a(0,n) + a(1,n)*k + a(2,n)*k^2 + ... a(q,n)*k^pp

where k is the lag and pp is the polynomial order.  Skipping some details,
Beta(n) can be learned by linearly transforming Sn(t,n) from a vector of
length K+1 to a vector, Zn(t,n), of length pp+1, and then doing normal
linear regression.  If we were to get further into the details, we would
find that the number of parameters to be estimated may be hugely reduced
(from K+1 to pp+1), as well as the dimension of the regression input.
Unfortunately, several reseachers have noted that polynomial space is not
expressive enough for many problems.

Another approach is to nonlinearly project the lags of Sn(t,n) onto a
B-spline basis.  During the regression estimation, the (spline) projection
coefficents can, again, be solved for linearly.  Skipping the details, we
can say that this roughly reduces the number of parameters to be estimated
from K+1 to ps+ks+1, where ps is the spline polynomial order and ks is the
number of knots.  After the transformation, the regression input dimension
increases slightly from K+1 to K+ks+1.

With either polynomial or spline lag projection, we could still use
penalized regression e.g. LASSO to select interesting sites and to
appropriately weight interesting lags.

Similarly, we also could project wind direction, economically producing a
direction-dependent regression weight for wind speed.  To enforce
continuity between angles 0 and 2*PI, periodic polynomials or splines could
be used, or alternatively, circular harmonic basis functions.

By forming a tensor product of the lag and direction projections, we could
again use standard least squares techniques to solve for the coefficients
during linear regression.

PROBLEMS WITH TENSOR PRODUCT OF MARGINALS

But there are problems with tensor products of the marginals

1.) Researchers have found that, while tensor products fit well at the
intersection of the one dimensional splines, they don't interpolate well.

2.) I have ignored the nonlinear relationship between speed and power.

3.) I could nonlinearly project speed with yet another spline and form the
tensor product with projected lag and direction.  But not only would this
greatly increase the number of parameters but it would increase the
probems with interpolation.

ADVICE NEEDED

I know that wavelets are another possible basis choice but I don't have
experience using them in more than one dimension.  More importantly, I have
never tried to tie them into a regression problem.  Before I implement
anthing, I thought I'd ask for advice from someone with expertise in this
area:

1.) Generally, is there a way to create 3-D function (regression
contribution at (speed,direction,lag)) that can be parameterized as a
linear combination of wavelet bases?

2.) Do you see an advantage to such an approach? Or is there some other
more appropriate choice?

3.) Papers (Chen?) suggest that expressing wavelet basis functions as full
vectors for each level of detail, and then thinning them with LASSO, produces
inaccurate wavelet coefficients.  Reconstruction is still OK but it seems
like this would decrease the learned regression function's generizablity
over unseen data.  Do you think it would?

4.) It would be straightforward to project wind direction with a scalar
periodic wavelet basis.  But would it be better to express wind velocity
with a complex number (speed,direction) and then work with analytic
wavelets?

5.) Are there 3D wavelet techniques that would work here that don't involve
tensor products?  If not, in your opinon, are tensor products OK?

Thanks,

Scott

******* wind speed

        ==> wind speed is a feature would help nn pick the right delay in
        a delay window.

********* TODO is this forecasted wind, wind at site or wind at measurement?  ask mark
******* pressure difference
        lags (delays) depend upon wind speed and /pressure difference/: [[file:energy.bib::bpa07inhourbalancerqt][bpa: in hour balancing]]

        ==> delta pressure as a feature would help nn pick the right delay in
        a delay window.  it would also be a low-dim feature, unlike
        correlation vs. lag
******* correlation / mutual information vs. lag

        the correlation/semblance/mi whatever for a given bin helps nn pick
        the right delay in a delay window.  this could be a pretty high dim
        feature unless subsample or just give correlation at forecast horizon
        lag only (and maybe no other lagged wind speed measurements either?)

******* scatterometry for wind
********* used in norsewind ([[file:energy.bib::oldroyd08norsewindrep1][oldroyd 2008: norsewind year periodic report]])
********* good [[http://www.coaps.fsu.edu/scatterometry/about/overview.php][quick explanation]]
********* can detect direction (sar needs help from nwp or something)
********* how much power returned is a function of wind speed and direction
********* observe from multiple angles and find speed/dir that best fits data
*********** if one beam, incident beam angles span 90 deg in ~ 5 mins, as satellite moves
          * ==> poor spatial resolution, i suppose
*********** can be ambiguous: fixing this is called "ambiguity selection"
*********** can also get 3 simultaneous angles w/ 3 antennae, as in the [[http://earth.esa.int/ers/eeo4.10075/scatt_design.html][esa earthnet design]]
******* SAR vs. Scatterometry
********* sar has higher spatial resolution
********* sar doesn't retrieve direction (w/o extra tricks)
********* sar focuses on a tight square, one angle
        * scatterometers sweep w/ wide beams, at multiple angles (3 in [[http://earth.esa.int/ers/eeo4.10075/scatt_design.html][esa earthnet design]])
        * is wind /speed/ accuracy about the same?

***** <<Power curve learning>>
******* <<Physics-based power curve features>>

         Provide them as options to an NN, let feature selection pick the
         best.  Alternatively, they could be turned into
          [[Multivariate base learners for boosting]] and chosen with
          [[Continuous Output Boosting]]

          The values that could be used to compose these features are at least:

          *AMMEND TO INCLUDE PITCH ANGLE (ReWP) as in [[file:energy.bib::Lydia13powCurvModelAdvncd][Lydia et al. 2013: Advanced Algorithms Wind]])*
          (mention how this produce could be logged to make angle, etc. additive, dep on speed could still be a 1D spline if but in log domain.  These could actually /all/ be spline base learners, added up)
          [[file:energy.bib::Juban07ProbWndFrcstFeatSelKDE][Juban et al. 2007: Probabilistic]] frcst: MI feat sel test humidity, etc. Also [[file:energy.bib::Lee14PowerCurveEstimation][Lee et al. 2014: Power Curve Estimation]] like (density, turbulence intensity wind shear).  Also, [[cite:Bai16condCplaWindPowCrvFeat][Bai et al. 2016 Cond. Copula wind Pow curve and feats]] has "wind elevation??"

          1. rho = B/R0/T (density)
          2. B (pressure)
          3. T (temperature, supposed to be good for ramps, see [[File:energy.bib::reikard08tempstaterampwind][Reikard 2008: Using Temperature...]])
          4. rho*v^3 (from P = 1/2 * rho * A * v^3)
          5. v^3
          6. direction
          7. stability or [[Wind power features besides spd/dir]]

         *Air density*

         From [[file:energy.bib::Wan10equivWindPowCurve][Wan et al. 2010: Development Equivalent Wind]], it's:

         rho = B/R0/T

         B:  pressure in Pascals (=100 mBar)
         R0: gas constant of dry air (287.06)
         T: temp in Kelvin (degrees C + 273)

         Note that Wan says that density didn't help much w/ a
         neural net power curve (also [[file:energy.bib::Li01neuralWindPowGen][Li et al. 2001: Using]])

         *Power curve*

         From [[file:energy.bib::Kalmikov11windPowFmdmntls][Kalmikov et al. 2011: Wind Power Fundamentals]], it's:

         P = 1/2 * rho * A * v^3

         rho: air density (see above)
         A: blade swept area (pi*r^2)
         v: wind velocity

         I [[file:d:/WLmesh/school/REMENAgridInt/REMENA_2012/homework/lecture5hw/Assignment%20and%20Solution/windspeedpdfPlot.m][played with Weibull wind speed]] in my 2012 REMENA class

         *Could also do log-log transform* for spd/pow relationship
         ([[file:energy.bib::Simonoff09transfRegrsn][Simonoff 2009: Transformations]] or others [[file:energy.bib::Gill01interpIntrctHierGLM][Gill 2001: Interpreting]])

         *Physics-based direction-power features*

         Assume the power/direction relationship is a multplicative
         function of angle:

         P(w=2*pi*theta/260) = P * f(w)

         Make f(w) a Fourier series in angle:  cos(w*k)+jsin(w*k) for a lot of k's making a Fourier kernel (see [[file:energy.bib::Kaufman05perSplnRgrsn][Kaufman et al. 2005: Spline]]):

         P(w) = sum(alpha(k)*K(w(k)*w))

         where w(k) is some discrete angle in the kernel.  To see why more
         than one freq is necessary, see [[why not sin/cos?]].  Next, make a
         regression input, you'd have sin/cos terms as inputs for each k

         input(k) = P * cos(k*w) ([[file:energy.bib::Kaufman05perSplnRgrsn][Kaufman et al. 2005: Spline]] has no sin())

         and let the regression figure out alpha(k).  P would come from any
         of the Power-like features mentioned above.

         This expansion could also be on wavelets or [[Periodic Splines]] or a
         [[Periodic Wavelet]] or both ([[file:energy.bib::Kapl09tensSplnWvlt][Kapl & J\uttler 2009]]).

         This could be a lot of k's (although [[file:energy.bib::Pritchard10varQuantProbFrcst][Pritchard 2010: Short]] says
         k=2 is OK for sin/cos, [[file:energy.bib::Marx10varyCoeffPsplineCmplx][Marx 2010: P]] also uses only 2) so could do
         PCA assuming a smooth relationship between the Fourier basis.
         Some kind of functional PCA is good: (This is mentioned in
         [[file:energy.bib::Aguilera13psplinePCA][Aguilera & Aguilera-Morillo 2013: Penalized PCA B]]).  A promising
         type is: [[file:energy.bib::Lu09UncorrMultiLinPCA][Lu et al. 2009: Uncorrelated Multilinear Principal]] (has
         Matlab)

         *Stability, etc.  eg.*

         [[file:energy.bib::Heller14PredWindPowGtAcc][Heller 2014: Predicting Wind Power Greater Accuracy]] stability & power curve, shading
         But I have many others bibteked and in this .org file. Should
         organize them better...

         [[cite:Bai16condCplaWindPowCrvFeat][Bai et al. 2016 Cond. Copula wind Pow curve and feats]] selected form of inputs e.g. pressure using [[Conditional Copulas]], also had prob-forecast-specific features.

         A simple proxy for stability/wake effects:  [[cite:Mittelmeier17powStdRatioWake][Mittelmeier et al. 2017: SCADA data pow std ratio wake]]

******* Learning montonicity
        <<Learning montonicity>>

        Maybe important for power curve learning, since an ideal power
        curve is monotonic (/except for beyond cutoff/).  Also good for
        learning cdf's or quantiles, since they must also be monotonic.

********* montonicity with splines: [[http://www.psych.mcgill.ca/misc/fda/ex-growth-d1.html][intro]] text and [[http://www.psych.mcgill.ca/misc/fda/ex-growth-d2.html][example]]
********* p. 11, [[file:energy.bib::Ramsay08funcAnalNotes][Ramsay 2008: Notes Functional]]
********* smooth.monotone() in the [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/fda/fda.pdf][R fda package]] should work for this
********* use montonicity in [[Functional Data Analysis]] regression?
*********** (p. 23, [[file:energy.bib::Ramsay08funcAnalNotes][Ramsay 2008: Notes Functional]])
*********** example 2. in [[file:~/lib/R/x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu/2.12/fda/demo/growth.R::f%20x%20b_0%20b_1%20D%201%20exp%20W%20x][fda/demo/growth.R]]
*********** I don't know yet how to do this in regression, though

********* Quantile Regression w/ monotonicity & other constraints: [[file:energy.bib::Kim06quantRgrsnShapeConstr][Kim 2006: Quantile Regression With]]
          (note that there's a quantile regression component somewhere in
          there, I think)
********* [[file:energy.bib::Demetriou02lsqFitMonoConv][Demetriou 2002: Signs]] (Least squares fitting with monotonicity/convexity constraint)

          Maybe relevant to optimal spinning reserves project, where we need to
          estimate the cost of reserves.  The idea was to empirically derive
          the cost curve market data.  This has to be monotonically increasing
          with reserve size.  This method could enforce that.

          He's written some fortran to do this.

********* Dispatch by learning montone functions: [[file:energy.bib::Lai05partSwarmDispNonSmth][Lai et al. 2005: Particle]] swarm non-smooth
********* [[file:energy.bib::Bollaerts06psplineSimpMultiShape][Bollaerts et al. 2006: Simple P]] splines, multivariate, shape constr
********* [[file:energy.bib::Eilers15twentyYrsPspline][Eilers et al. 2015: Twenty P]]splines review
********* [[file:energy.bib::Lyche05SplineMethodsLecNts][Lyche & Moerken 2005: Spline Methods]]: UoOslo Spline course lectures
********* [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/fileexchange/24443-slm-shape-language-modeling][SLM - Shape Language Modeling]]: Matlab library
*********** has monotonic regression
*********** but requires optimization toolbox
*********** doesn't do penalized splines.  But can pick knots
********* [[file:energy.bib::Pya15shapeCnstrAddMdl][Pya & Wood 2015: Shape]] constrained add models, multivar, mono, pnlty.
********* [[file:energy.bib::Kagerer13splnLSQregrssnIntro][Kagerer 2013]] intro to splines has constraint matrix equs.
********* [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/fileexchange/25872-free-knot-spline-approximation][Free-knot spline approximation]]: matlab code
*********** it required [[http://sigpromu.org/projects.html#quadprog][QPC library]], and I couldn't get the mex files to work on my 64 bit laptop
*********** can specify lower and upper bounds on derivative
*********** seems to remove knots if not needed
********* [[file:energy.bib::Meyer00degFreedomShpCnstr][Meyer & Woodroofe 2000: Degrees Freedom Shape Restricted Regression]]
********* Linear quantile spline w/ mono/other constraints: p. 332, [[file:energy.bib::Koenker05QuantRgrssnBook][Koenker 2005: Quantile]]
********* [[http://www.mai.liu.se/~olbur/PROJECTS/isot_regr.html][Isotonic Regression]] project
********* [[http://www.mathworks.com/help/techdoc/ref/pchip.html][Matlab's builtin: pchip()]] is mono _if training data is purely monotonic_
*********** montonicity is ensured when the training data is monotonic
************* won't get polynomial-type ringing at sharp edges
*********** from: [[file:energy.bib::Ableson12classNotesMonoSpline][Ableson: Applications Numerical Methods Lecture]] (monotone matlab, pchip)
************* estimates ‘reasonable’ derivatives at each control point
************* has a zero derivative if the control point is a local (data) max or min
************* These two things guarantee that the interpolation will be locally monotone. The
********* just sorting can work: [[file:energy.bib::Chernozhukov10qrNoCross][Chernozhukov et al. 2010: Quantile Probability Curves Without Crossing]]
********* using erf() function and optimization toolbox
*********** [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/newsreader/view_thread/34206][matlab code]], requires optimization toolbox

********* spatial statistical interpolation ("kriging")
********* forecasting
*********** no notion of "time" so how forecast ahead?
*********** worry: GP's maybe not as good for monotonic trends
            From [[file:energy.bib::Tancret99CompNeuralGaussProcAlloy][Tancret et al. 1999: Comparison of artificial]] GP's will
            extend trends for a litle bit, but decay to a default b/c of
            Gaussian covariance decay w/ length scale.  So, NN's may BE
            better for monotonic trends!  See also: [[Learning montonicity]]
*********** but people do it.  See:

***** Multiplicative Process Estimation
      <<Multiplicative Process Estimation>>
******* fractal dimension in wind forecasting: [[file:energy.bib::reikard08tempstaterampwind][reikard 2008: using temperature and]]
********* result of multiplicative processing
********* says no known alg. for this
********* todo look up multiplicative process estimation (i've seen in paper titles)
********* todo also, what about dynamical system w/ lag embedding?  doesn't this handle?
******* Box-Cox lambda can adjust between multipicative and additive relationship
        From [[https://www.otexts.org/fpp/6/5][here]] (this is the site of this book: [[file:energy.bib::Hyndman14Forecastingprinciplesand][Hyndman & Athanasopoulos 2014: Forecasting]]):

          It is possible to obtain a multiplicative decomposition by first
          taking logs of the data, and then back-transforming the
          components. Decompositions some way between additive and
          multiplicative can be obtained using a Box-Cox transformation of
          the data with 0<λ<1. A value of λ=0 corresponds to the
          multiplicative decomposition while λ=1 is equivalent to an additive
          decomposition.

       Lambda picking: [[file:energy.bib::Unknown13boxCoxSeasonal][Unknown 2013: Research Paper]] on Box-Cox seasonal

******* TODO PV compared to Wind/Load[[file:energy.bib::Forbes11pvWindRelTenneT][: Forbes et al. 2011: Do Higher PV]]
******* higher than expected wind means both more power from both wind and PV

        Wind cooling is a way in which wind and PV power forecast errors
        could be correlated: Wind cools PV, increasing their efficiency and
        output. If high winds are not predicted, both wind a PV would produce
        more than forecast ([[https://www.evernote.com/edit/1e7a8542-1de7-46e0-95ae-ce2be6af52d2?shard%3Ds13&csrfBusterToken%3D8ff0d2cf#st%3Dp&n%3D1e7a8542-1de7-46e0-95ae-ce2be6af52d2][is seen in California]])
******* [[file:energy.bib::Zhang13windPVcorr][Zhang et al. 2013: Investigating Correlation Between]]

      <<wrap prob forecast algorithm inside ensemble bma em loop>>

      *idea* would be to insert prob forecast algorithm inside of bma em
      loop.

      e.g. uses unconditional error dist: [[file:energy.bib::courtney13frcstbayavg][courtney et al. 2013: high bayesian]]
      (see p. 3 of the paper, and my comments)


      in courtney, they use distribution that doesn't depend upon past
      values, predicted current value, etc.  seems that it be better to
      use a real probabilistic forecast w/ conditional densities
      e.g. pierre or andre'

      might work if it can be squeezed its em, seems easy via weighting of
      training examples , like i tried nn confidence values.

      note: my nn confidence/ thing could also handle missing features for
      ensemble and prob forecastsl

***** Super Quantiles

      Prediction the average cost in the upper tail of a distribution.
      Useful for tractable optimization, is additive, and conservative.
      Seems relevant to regulation power determination and stochastic
      optimization.

        | aspect                   | [[file:energy.bib::pinson09probfrcststatscenwind][pinson09]]               | [[file:energy.bib::morales10scenarios][morales10]]              |
        |--------------------------+------------------------+------------------------|
        | autocorrelation          | covar. matrix has lags | arma on marginals      |
        | parm estimated           | power                  | wind speed             |
        | dependence               | linear, multivar norm. | linear, multivar norm. |
        | multi-var norm. mistake? | yes                    | yes                    |
        | stationarity             | adaptive cov.          | ignored                |
        | joint lag dependence     | full multi-var cov.    | arma noise input cov.  |
        | marginal distribution    | weird power dist.      | weibull                |
        |                          |                        |                        |

******* scenario tree reduction

********* optimization problem:

          r = renewable generation (prob.)
          g = conventional power production schedule (determ.)
          c = constraints (ramp constraints, demand control limits).
          d = power demand without any demand control (prob.)
          d = demand response attempted demand adjustment (prob.)

          problem statement:

          find:         g*,d* = argmin cost(r,g,d,d*)
                                 g,d

          constraints:  d+d <= r+g (over all time)
                        c satsified (with some probability?)

********* why scenario trees?

          o d,g have temporal dependence (constraints on ramps,
            time-of-day, etc.)
          o energy storage will add temporal dependence
          o uncertainty in forecast of r increases with time

          ==> each decision on g,d affects future decisions
          ==> instead of just k combinations of d,g decisions to optimize
              at at each time step, it's k^t combinations over t time
              steps into the future.

          but... it's not totally crazy because constraints (like ramps)
          will eliminate many paths and the probabilities of
          certain scenarios will drop to zero over time.

          ==> maybe could do viterbi pruning, like in hmm's
              with a fixed bandwidth.

              o but: this could exclude [[Extreme Quantile Forecasting]], even if
                uncertainties are correctly modeled (extreme events are
                always low probability).
              o maybe keep track of excluded probability mass, turning
                beamwidth from a finite number of paths being tracked to
                a width of probability being counted?  surely, somebody's
                thought of this before.

          ==> maybe /merge/ redundant scenarios instead of /pruning/ low prob scenarios

********* probabilistic view

          trying to produce a distribution of demand/production (or
          strorage retrieval) error that has some tiny probability of
          insufficiency at each step.

********* [[Scenario/Ensemble quality metrics]]
********* some kinda [[submodular optimization]]?
*********** unit commitment problem is a mixed integer opt. prob.
************* "probabilistic mixed integer?"
************* otherwise, replaces linear optimization approaches?
************* from the [[submodular tutorial slides]], some functions of submodular functions are also submodular
************* does this mean that scenario reduction can become submodular (and thus more tractable)
************* there are online submodular optimization methods: help w/ beam?

              the viterbi beam limiting idea may be kind of dumb; can an
              online submod opt. method (see: [[submodular tutorial slides]])
              be smarter somehow?

************* submod combined across time steps

              seems like it could almost be just setting states of
              everything across t, then estimating the cost, like with
              the water contamination problem in the [[submodular tutorial slides]].

*********** mixed integer programming is submodular: see [[submodular tutorial slides]]
*********** scenario tree reduction anything lke minimal cost information cascades in [[submodular tutorial slides]]
*********** e.g. bilmes's paper: [[http://ssli.ee.washington.edu/~bilmes//pgs/sort_date.html][online algorithms for submodular minimization with combinatorial constraints]]
*********** see paper?: "on submodular value functions of dynamic programming"

***** bounding by output transformation or modeling
      <<Bounding by output transformation>>

      For wind power, logit() seems popular and also settled on in
      [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes06compQuantileWind][Bremnes 2006]], where the author tried both.

******* sqrt: ensure non-negative output: predict square-root instead
        then, when square, it's always positive.  this was a trick proposed
        by gary king, the amelia ii author
********* king's email from the amelia ii listserv:

for the first, you can use the square root transformation. for the second, rounding i'm sure will be fine.


gary
