on sat, oct 22, 2011 at 2:19 pm, sera choma <sera.onalan@gmail.com> wrote:

hi,

i would like to set bounds for some of my variables. for example i have a
variable that measures the number of health personnel in a given province.
the min should be 0, but i do not require a max bound. what would be the
best approach for this type of bound? should i be setting the max to
infinity?

also, i have set a bound for one of my dependent variables that is a
percentage of votes in a given province. the min is 0 and the max is 1.
however, when i impute my data the min for this variable is -1.388e-17,
which is nearly 0. i am not sure why this happens and if it is ok for me to
keep a negative number (even though it is so small) as my dependent variable
(that is a proportion). any suggestions?

thank you for your help.

sera
******* arcsin(sqrt(x/powMax)): [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes04windLocQR][Bremnes 2004: Probabilistic]]
******* logit "logistic" xform, asin or probit are possibilties: [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes06compQuantileWind][Bremnes 2006]]: probabilistic comparison

        Calls it the "logistic" function but transform is  [[https://personality-project.org/r/psych/help/logistic.html][really a
        logit()]]; the untransform _after_ regression is logistic.

******* logit SDE xform: [[file:energy.bib::Moller13windFrcstSDE][Moeller et al. 2013: Probabilistic Forecasts Wind]]
******* [[Beta regression]]
******* [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kumaraswamy_distribution][Kumaraswamy Distribution]]
******* ensure non-negative w/ log (Matlab ksdensity)

        for example, see the [[http://www.mathworks.de/help/toolbox/stats/ksdensity.html][help]] for the matlab ksdensity function:

        if the support parameter is 'positive', ksdensity transforms x
        using a log function, estimates the density of the transformed
        values, and transforms back to the original scale. if support is a
        vector [l u], ksdensity uses the transformation
        log((x-l)/(u-x)). the width parameter and u outputs are on the
        scale of the transformed values.

******* double bounded, many others [[file:energy.bib::Fink09xformFAQs][Fink 2009: FAQs]]
******* many link functions (p. 103): [[file:energy.bib::Madsen11glmBook][Madsen & Thyregod 2011: Introduction]]
******* link functions w/ good plots: [[file:energy.bib::Fox08glmBookChap][Fox 2008: Applied Regression Analysis]]
******* many: [[file:energy.bib::Simonoff09transfRegrsn][Simonoff 2009: Transformations]], plus what relationship is implied
******* [[file:energy.bib::Wang13extrmQRpowTranf][Wang & Li 2013: Estimation Extreme Conditional]] lin w/ nonlinear tails, tail test
******* [[file:energy.bib::Gill01interpIntrctHierGLM][Gill 2001: Interpreting]] interactions, GLM

******* [[file:energy.bib::Ahmed10empCompForecast][Ahmed et al. 2010]] machine time series
******* [[file:energy.bib::Pinson12vShrtWndPowLogitNorm][Pinson 2012: Very]] short term prob frcst logit-normal
******* [[file:energy.bib::Mauch13windPowFrcstLogitNorm][Mauch et al. 2013]] logit norm quantile wind power
******* [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truncated_normal_distribution][Truncated Normal Distribution]]
******* Truncated normal distribution can be created w/ a Power transformation
********* i.e. can produce the [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Box%25E2%2580%2593Cox_distribution][Box-Cox distribution]] (where f=1)
********* Box-Cox dist is nice b/c it's continuous (easy to learn?)
********* Do xform w/ [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_transform][Power Transform]], one instance of which is the Box-Cox transform
          Box-Cox transform is often used to make things more
          Gaussianized.  To "stabilize" the variance (I think), which means
          that it doesn't change w/ the mean (I think).
    <<Improving P&K Cond. Pred. Int.>>

*** Effect of precipitation
    <<Effect of precipitation>>
***** rain
******* rain reduces wind speed
        from christof:

        translation of german abstract: the fall of raindrops can bind so
        much energy that by the atmospheric circulation could be slowed
        down considerably. this is the result of a recent study by american
        scientists. researchers have estimated the atmosphere in it for the
        first time, how much is due to friction forces caused by braking
        effect when rain falls within an air flow. drag forces deform and
        slow the rain drops during their fall and thus ensure that they
        fall at a certain speed. this is also for the air masses associated
        to a significant loss of kinetic energy. in a broad band between 30
        degrees north and south latitude, ie an area of approximately from
        north to south africa amounts to enough energy that the air mass is
        removed through the rain, about 1.8 watts per square meter,
        according to the researchers. the effect would be sufficient, so in
        regions where increasing due to climate change the rainfall,
        subdued the wind power or other atmospheric movement patterns could
        be disrupted.

        paul olivier, juliana dias: satellite estimates of precipitation-induced
        dissipation in the atmosphere, science, 24 february 2012, vol 335
        (6071), p. 953-956

*** Grid node forecast
    Estimating power at grid nodes in a way that has spatial dependence in
    time like real RES feedin.  In other words, it's forecasting a _vector_,
    not power at each point individually

******* [[file:energy.bib::Davidson15InsideDOEsWindFrcst][Davidson 2015: Inside DOE]] wind frcsting effort

        A comprehensive list of relevant topography-related phenomena that
        are poorly represented in models includes warm fronts in stable
        atomospheric conditions, gap flows, mountain waves, topographic
        wakes, convective outflows, marine pushes, land-sea breezes, slope
        and drainage flows, and low-level jets.

*** <<Fourier Based Missing Value Fill-In>>
***** for forecasting, may prefer dct to dft
******* [[http://www0.cs.ucl.ac.uk/teaching/gz05/03-fourier.pdf][dct has smoother periodic extension]] (so missing rhs less of a problem)
******* dct expresses more in fewer coeffs, means smaller covariance matrix dimension
******* reconstruction is smoother: [[file:energy.bib::blinn93dealdct][blinn 1993: whats dct]]
***** or may prefer wavelets
******* localized in both time and freq: [[http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/pmc3149002/][better for truncated data than dft]]
***** [[file:energy.bib::][asari 2005: technical notes linear:]] svd, ridge regression, fourier basis
***** idea:

      could [[use direct dft to estimate ft of partly missing features]] on 1-d
      signals, and then do regression across their dft coeffs.

      *how to do em*: latent variables are still in time domain, but
      they're transformed to freq domain before likelihood
      calculation (based on multi-dim regression or var (needed if
      doing dft, which captures autocorr?).  this will further
      increase dimensions, so could do another linear transform w/
      svd (and this could be incremental so could adapt to
      conditions.  see bayesian pca or incremental svd).  there is em
      can adapt in time, bayesian adaptation or something like that.

      might be relevant to em:
      http://www2.ece.ohio-state.edu/~schniter/pdf/ciss12_em_slides.pdf

      but can we do a [[bayesian%20fft][bayesian fft?]]

      bootstrap is still in frequency domain, though to avoid block
      bootstrap or whatever.

      foreach d (d in dims with missing points)
        x1d(d,:) = dftwithmissingdatatrick(x(d,:))

      could also use approach like these:
      [[file:energy.bib::kirch11timefreqbtstrp][kirch & politis 2011: tft]] bootstrap (better jornsten)
      [[file:energy.bib::brooks12fouriermissfill][brooks et al. 2012: fitting multitemporal curve]]:  linear interp

      note: [[fourier fill-in signal has to be bandlimited, sufficiently sampled]]
      /spectral smoothing is not quite the same thing.../  also,
      there's an issue with fft analysis window edges, where fft
      assumes periodic extension (blurring).  a way to get rid of it
      is to taper but that /deletes/ the edge points, so can't do that.

      then, do [[simple whitening bootstrap in freq domain]] to get many
      samples:

      x --> dft --> whiten --> ift --> random sample --> dft --> unwhiten
	--> ift --> one bootstrap sample (a possible vector of data
                                          in a gap)

      maybe use [[file:energy.bib::smaragdis11timefreqimpute][smaragdis et al. 2011: missing]] to pick best phase.

      *questions*:

      1. what sort of a var relationship is assumed by an n-dim fft?
      2. what kind of relationship is spectral smoothing assuming?
      3. what is the whitening doing?
      4. what does the n-dim dft of stripes of delayed and scaled
         signals look like?
      5. how to handle non-stationarity?
      6. how to do n-dim spectral smoothing? just average
      7. how to do n-dim tapers or multi-tapers?  or is that necessary?
      8. how related is this idea to [[file:energy.bib::kirch11timefreqbtstrp][kirch & politis 2011: tft]] ?

******* todo read [[file:energy.bib::smaragdis11timefreqimpute][smaragdis et al. 2011: missing]] for clue on how to do em iteration
******* todo look up "rolling em" or sliding window em or something like that.

******* todo refs for incremental svd and bayesian pca
********* lot's of stuff in stored chrome windows
********* [[http://bibliotheques.univ-toulouse.fr/archipelplus/details/fetch-logical-g958-837db10e0860a98ec8faccb3309a43a331d83fdbf946149b4218735659e2fd051][incremental expectation maximization principal component analysis for missing value imputation for coevolving eeg data]]
********* [[http://bibliotheques.univ-toulouse.fr/archipelplus/details/fetch-logical-c1613-c3b7a70e970b954330330803aec0ad9e8cab3c71fddb61e8c38e5386719c45e41][wavelet based multiresolution expectation maximization image reconstruction algorithm for positron emission tomography]]
***** bad idea: multidimensional dft

      *can't do multidimensional dft*: across time, you can assume
      smoothness for fft but not across strips of different kinds of
      measurements in no particular order.  perhaps you could arrange
      them so that their orders match their spatial arrangements
      (mdl) but time shifts and different measurement types (wind
      speed/dir/pressure) are going to ensure discontinuities.

      fft's are ortogonal so can just do one-dim fft's or dft's and
      then do and fft (see [[http://www.mathcs.org/java/programs/fft/fftinfo/c12-4.pdf][here]]). [[use direct dft to estimate ft of partly missing features]] on 1-d
      signals, then fft again for n-dim ft:

      foreach d (d in dims with missing points)
        x1d(d,:) = dftwithmissingdatatrick(x(d,:))

      foreach k=1:nfft
        xnd(:,k) = fft(x1d(:,k))

      calc many xnd's and average to smooth.  averaging could be done
      by clustering?  xnd could be stored and retrieved based on best
      match with current spectrum.

      note: [[fourier fill-in signal has to be bandlimited, sufficiently sampled]]
      /spectral smoothing is not quite the same thing.../  also,
      there's an issue with fft analysis window edges, where fft
      assumes periodic extension (blurring).  a way to get rid of it
      is to taper but that /deletes/ the edge points, so can't do that.

      then, do [[simple whitening bootstrap in freq domain]] to get many
      samples:

      x --> dft --> whiten --> ift --> random sample --> dft --> unwhiten
	--> ift --> one bootstrap sample

      maybe use [[file:energy.bib::smaragdis11timefreqimpute][smaragdis et al. 2011: missing]] to pick best phase.

      *questions*:

      1. what sort of a var relationship is assumed by an n-dim fft?
      2. what kind of relationship is spectral smoothing assuming?
      3. what is the whitening doing?
      4. what does the n-dim dft of stripes of delayed and scaled
         signals look like?
      5. how to handle non-stationarity?
      6. how to do n-dim spectral smoothing? just average
      7. how to do n-dim tapers or multi-tapers?  or is that necessary?
      8. how related is this idea to [[file:energy.bib::kirch11timefreqbtstrp][kirch & politis 2011: tft]] ?

***** [[http://books.nips.cc/papers/files/nips16/nips2003_aa55.pdf][generalised propagation for fast fourier transforms with partial or missing features]]
***** [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/stamp/stamp.jsp?arnumber%3d00003925][constrained fourier space method for compensation of missing features in emission computed tomography]]
******* [[http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18230450][pub med page]]
***** [[http://www.mathworks.com/matlabcentral/newsreader/view_thread/105116][use direct dft to estimate ft of partly missing features]] (matlab)
      <<use direct dft to estimate ft of partly missing features>>

      use this to either fill-in time points (just do inverse dft),
      or to select historical spectra which match the estimated one
      to somehow form templates from which bootstrap estimates can be
      performed.

      *question*: is this better or worse than the linear interpolation
      trick in [[file:energy.bib::brooks12fouriermissfill][brooks et al. 2012: fitting multitemporal curve]]?

      answer might be found in this [[http://asmedl.org/getabs/servlet/getabsservlet?prog%3dnormal&id%3djseedo000128000002000226000001&idtype%3dcvips&gifs%3dyes&ref%3dno][paper]]:

        study of cubic splines and fourier series as interpolation
        techniques for filling in short periods of missing building
        energy use and weather data

******* matlab

> here's aj johnson's contribution to that thread::
>
> to cut to the chase, as they say, here is the code.
> cheers! -aj
>
> function x=dft(t,x,f)
> % function x=dft(t,x,f)
> % compute dft (discrete fourier transform) at frequencies given
> % in f, given samples x taken at times t:
> % x(f) = sum { x(k) * e**(2*pi*j*t(k)*f) }
> % k
>
> t = t(:); % format 't' into a column vector
> x = x(:); % format 'x' into a column vector
> f = f(:); % format 'f' into a column vector
>
> % it's just this simple:
> w = exp( 2*pi*j * f*t');
> x = w * x;

later corrected by greg heath:
 w = exp(-2*pi*j * f*t'); % i.e., notice the minus sign

***** fourier fill-in signal has to be [[http://www.physicsforums.com/showthread.php?t%3d613349][bandlimited, sufficiently sampled]]
      <<fourier fill-in signal has to be bandlimited, sufficiently sampled>>

***** Low level jets
      From: [[cite:Laing11introTropMeteo][Laing & Evans 2011: Introduction Tropical Meteo]]

Low-level jets (LLJs) are regional wind maxima in the lower troposphere that are defined by Stensrud (1996)122 as follows:

Narrow area of maximum in wind speed below 700 hPa
Vertical wind profile with speed increasing to the jet core and decreasing above
Horizontal wind shear exist on side of the jet, e.g., weaker winds at the edge of the jet

>>> Malte Jansen 3/12/2015 4:16 pm >>>

You've got the right person

1. Re: K:\Organisation\Daten\EEX\Spot_market
  1.Day-Ahead and Intraday (several files)
  2.EUR/MWh for price and MWh for Energy
  3.Someone (I think Patrick) already converted them into Matlab, however only prices, not the volumes. Should be on the drive as well.
2. Re: For sure, the intraday prices are online.
  1. Are available in the very same folder
  2. The intraday price is merely just one price component. I use the average price. However this is debatable. Probably better to use a mixture between last price and average price.
3.Re: reserve settlement price. I have never seen those prices. Might be actually for the Dutch business branch of TenneT. TenneT is grid operator in the Netherlands. Also looks like the imbalance settlement price that has to be paid by the balance responsible parties
  1.I don't have that data.
  2.The data I used was from

  https://www.regelleistung.net/ip/action/index?language=en. I've already
  downloaded it and it should be available in Matlab. Not sure about the
  time frame but starting in 2010 and until 2014 should be available

  3.Imbalances are paid for by the balance responsible parties. The price

  they pay is the imbalance settlement price (Ausgleichsenergiepreis)
  https://www.regelleistung.net/ip/action/static/chargesys. The prices are
  calculated on the energy costs of secondary and tertiary control reserve
  (plus some more adjustments to the price). Only BRPs are accountable for
  imbalances. If a single power plant in the portfolios doesn't deliver
  it'll be dealt with bilaterally

  4.I think it's the Dutch prices. Imbalance prices in Germany are symmetric, and ...

  5.uniform for all 4 TSOs
  6.In my understanding it's an additional price component. A similar price component has been introduced in the German Ausgleichsenergiepreis. It shall encourage the performance of the BRPs by introducing an element of fear for high prices.
4.Re: reconciliation price. Don't know what that is. Definitely no applicable in Germany. Only go for the Ausgleichsenergiepreis

Hope I could help you

Malte

>>> Scott Otterson 12.03.2015 15:01 >>>

Hi Malte,

Sorry to repeat a questions you've probably heard several times before, but here they are again...  Do you have time to answer them or is there a better person?

Questions

1.We've got some kind of data in:

  K:\Organisation\Daten\EEX\Spot_market

  1.Are these day ahead prices?
  2.Whatever they are, what are the units?
  3.If they aren't day-ahead, do you know where to find day-ahead?
2.For sure, the intraday prices are online.
  1.Has this been downloaded to IWES?
  2.If this is the data you used for your ancillary service papers, how did you simulate the price paid to bidders using the hourly low/high/last prices in this data set?
3.It looks like reserve settlement prices are available online.
  1.Has anybody downloaded it?
  2.Is this the data you used for your dynamic reserve allocation and ancillary services papers?
  3.You can tell me right now if the answers to these questions are in your German market report but...
    Who pays this price, and how is it distributed across the power providers who missed their bids? I don't mean the balance responsibles but the specific parties who have promised electricity and then didn't deliver it.
  4.It seems that the prices are asymmetric. Is this new?  If so, when did it start?
  5.Are the prices different for each TSO?
  6.When assessing the cost of forecast errors, how does the incentive component fit in?
4.Just to be sure, is the reconciliation price unrelated to production forecast error costs?

Thanks,

Scott

>>> Dominik Jost 3/13/2015 12:20 pm >>>

Hey Scott,

Here is the time-series of the imbalance-price from August 2013 till the
end of 2014.

The price multiplied with the imbalance energy the BRP consumes is what the
BRP has to pay to the TSO.

pos. imbalance price and BRP 'consumes'  imbalance energy --> TSO gets money from the BRP

pos. imbalance price and BRP ' produces' imbalance energy --> BRP gets money from the BRP

neg. imbalance price and BRP 'consumes' imbalance energy --> BRP gets money from the TSO

neg. imbalance price and BRP ' produces' imbalance energy --> TSO gets money from the BRP

Regarding the 15-min intraday prices I will have to ask Patrick on Monday
as he is the only one who can download the data from the EEX.

If you have got questions do not hesitate to ask me!

Dominik

******* Market Questions/Answers: Dominik Jost
********* Intraday
*********** Seller/buyer task
************* views: [[http://www.epexspot.com/en/market-data/intradaycontinuous/intraday-table/-/DE][15 min. realtime web page]] (but they see more)
************* This is updated as bids come in? YES, probably
************* Forecast horizon: time from "now" to a 15 min. period in table: YES
************* How much can the person buy or sell?
*************** Can _buy_ whatever _volume_ is being _sold?_ YES
*************** Can _sell_ whatever _volume_ is being _bought_? YES
*************** Or place an offer and find out? YES
*************** last price is last traded (45 mins b/f delivery)
*************** if not enough power, it's OTC or ancillary
************* [[https://www.epexspot.com/en/product-info/intradaycontinuous/germany][Trading rules]]
*************** Power tick: min increment is 0.1 MW.
*************** Price tick: minimum price increment is EUR 0.01 per MWh.
*************** Price range:s -9999€ - 9999€.
*************** Horizons: This is actually not very clear...

                Dominik Jost says: So horizons of max. 33 hours are
                theoretically possible. This is due to the fact that the
                Day-Ahead-Market closes at 12 a.m.

                o single hour periods: delivery on same or following day on
                  single hours,

                o 15-minute periods or on block of hours: Each hour,
                  15-minute periods or block of hours can be traded until
                  45 minutes before delivery begins.

                o Starting at _3pm_ on the current day, all _hours_ of the
                  following day can be traded.

                o Starting at _4pm_ on the current day, all _15-minute_ periods
                  of the following day can be traded.

************** Standardised blocks

               o Baseload covering hours 1 to 24
               o Peakload covering hours 9 to 20 on every week day (Mon-Fri)
               o Members also have the possibility to submit user-defined
                 blocks linking several consecutive hours of their choice.

************** Type of orders

               o [[file:energy.bib::Gould13limitOrderBks][Limit orders]]
               o Market Sweep Orders
               o 10th MW Orders
               o With execution restrictions: “Immediate-or-cancel” (IOC),
                “Fill-or-kill” (FOK), “All-or-none” (AON) or “Iceberg”.

************** Place of Delivery

               Deliveries are made within either of the following zones:

               Amprion GmbH
               TenneT TSO GmbH
               50Hertz Transmission GmbH
               TransnetBW GmbH

************** Trading hours

               Trading is continuous 7 days a week and 24 hours a day.

************** OTC trades

               Intraday OTC trades can also be registered for clearing
               through the trading system.

******* Why Bremnes/DTU quantile trading doesn't work for Germany
        <<Why Bremnes/DTU quantile trading doesn't work for Germany>>

Email to LNEG IRPWIND WP82.4 partner, CC'ed to Peder Bacher (DTU), IWES
people,...  The Bremnes algorithm is here: [[file:energy.bib::Bremnes04precipQuantsVerif][Bremnes 2004: Probabilistic NWP]]

>>> Scott Otterson 1/21/2016 2:54 PM >>>

Hi António,

Here's a quick note explaining why the Bremnes algorithm -- implemented in the DTU code -- isn't appropriate for the German market:

1.German laws don't allow speculating against balancing power, as would be
done by the Bremnes algorithm (I guess speculation is also not allowed in
the Danish market).  Recently, enforcement of the German rule has gotten
stricter [Garnier14blncErrIntraday.pdf].

2.German imbalance prices are symmetric
[VanderVeen10imbalSettleDEvsNL.pdf].  Asymmetry is a fundamental assumption
of the Bremnes algorithm implemented in the DTU code.

3.Almost all corrections to German day ahead forecast errors are done on
the intraday market; balancing power is only about 2.5% of wholesale market
[Hirth13balPowRnwblGerman.pdf].

4.The German balancing power prices are unknown until weeks after market
close  [VanderVeen10imbalSettleDEvsNL.pdf].  This breaks an even more
fundamental assumption of the Bremnes algorithm.

5.Balancing power prices are extremely difficult to forecast -- personal
communication and e.g. [Moehrlen12tradeStrtgyRESeeg2012.pdf]

At the moment, I don't know what to do.  But I'm thinking that there might
be a way to find asymmetry on the German intraday market, possibly via
considering liquidity.  I haven't gotten far with this yet, so if you have
ideas, I'm all ears.

Scott

******* TSO intraday correction trading rules: [[file:energy.bib::juris10VerordnungzurAusfuhrung][Verordnung Ausfuehrung Verordnung]] 2010

>>> Henry Martin 10/27/2016 5:27 pm >>>
Hey Scott,
there is a law and a regulation that specifies how exactly the law should be applied. And in this specification it says, "that the difference in between forecast and traded energy must be zero".

It says nothing about mean or median but I can understand the interpretation of the TSOs. I think what we should give them is a black box that does the forecast and spits out a value for the last trade which we would name something fancy (best expected trading decision or something ;-) ).

>>> Dominik Jost 10/17/2016 9:33 pm >>>
Dear Scott,

I finally rememered our short conversation about 3 weeks ago regarding the obligation for TSOs to sell the forecasted amount of wind and PV energy on the day-ahead and intraday market, respectively. I am very sorry to send you the link before but I totally forgot... Sorry!In AusglMechAV - which is the relevant regulation here and can be found here: https://www.gesetze-im-internet.de/ausglmechav/BJNR013400010.html - they say in §1 that the TSO have to sell the enerergy according to the forecasts in the DA- and finally in the ID-market and these forecasts have to be state-of-the-art.

Hope, that it still helps you!
Best,Dominik

********* Markus's comments

          Here are some paper, which migth be interesting for you.

          o The first two papers describe nearly the same method to
          calculate the control reserve. Both of them use this Reserve
          Management Tool. (Bessa and Matos)

          o a very interesting theme is: what mistake is responsible for
          which kind of frequency control (does the wind forecast error
          increase the amout of tertiary control or secondary
          control). There hasn´t been down so much research on this topic
          yet (I think due to the missing of data with such a high time
          resoution). Frunt deals with this question. (Frunt)

          o the actual method is described in consentec. Even though it is
          german, you might look on side 23. This gives a very comprehensiv
          overview of the method. (Consentec)

***** <<Submodular Optimization>>
******* Jeff Bilmes has done a lot on it
********* talked about this @ ASRU 2008 ([[http://ssli.ee.washington.edu/~bilmes/ee595a_spring_2011/lecture1.pdf][his SSLI slides]])
********* he has a [[http://ssli.ee.washington.edu/~bilmes//pgs/sort_date.html][ton of papers]] on the topic; most relevant to feature selection?:

          "An Application of the Submodular Principal Partition to
           Training Data Subset Selection."

          "Learning sparse models for a dynamic Bayesian network
           classifier of protein secondary structure."

          "How to Select a Good Training-data Subset for Transcription:
           Submodular Active Selection for Sequences"

********* his class: [[http://ssli.ee.washington.edu/~bilmes/ee595a_spring_2011/][EE595A]] - Submodular Functions, Their Optimization And Applications - Spring Quarter 2011
*********** book used for class: [[http://www.amazon.com/Submodular-Functions-Optimization-Discrete-Mathematics/dp/0444520864][Submodular Functions and Optimization]]
            <<book: Submodular Functions and Optimization>>
************* [[http://books.google.com/books/about/Submodular_Functions_and_Optimization.html?id%3DgdcRXdoV89QC&redir_esc%3Dy][google book search]]
*********** syllabus says you should know some convex optimization (some other survey paper said the same thing)
******* tutorial: [[file:energy.bib::Bach11lrnSubModCnvx][Bach 2011: Learning Submodular Functions]] Convex

        <<submodular tutorial slides>>

******* Uses of submodularity
********* Forecast aggregation (upscaling) by submodular optimization
          <<forecast aggregation by submodular optimization>>
          like the Ph Monitoring thing, where you're forecasting the whole
          surface but only pick a subset of the points to install sensors.
          (the surface is modeled with a Gaussian process)

          see also: [[Forecast aggregation]]

***** SDE's in Optimization
      <<SDE's in Optimization>>

      Henrik says stochastic differential equations make optimization
      tractible.  What evidence can I find of that?
******* Easy to handle? [[http://books.google.de/books?id%3D9lWjL2QLAkEC&pg%3DPA15&lpg%3DPA15&dq%3Dstochastic%2Bdifferential%2Bequations%2Boptimization&source%3Dbl&ots%3DX3U5_CWNgh&sig%3DHrah20au269LRsGbfL4e-ZA0q44&hl%3Den&sa%3DX&ei%3DfbZkVLW-Ls3faoLTgpAB&redir_esc%3Dy#v%3Donepage&q%3Dstochastic%2520differential%2520equations%2520optimization&f%3Dfalse][Passage]] from book "[[http://books.google.de/books?id%3D9lWjL2QLAkEC&dq%3Dstochastic%2Bdifferential%2Bequations%2Boptimization&source%3Dgbs_navlinks_s][Dynamic Economics : Optimization by the Lagrange Method]]"
******* They are used to model power systems: [[http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/xpl/articleDetails.jsp?arnumber%3D6547228][A Systematic Method to Model Power Systems as Stochastic Differential Algebraic Equations
        ]]But this seems to be electrical system transient analysis, not unit
        commitment, etc.

>>> Erika Kämpf 8/14/2017 9:44 AM >>>
Hello everybody,

The Guideline system operation will be valid throughout Europe and will mainly concern:

◾TSOs,


◾Transmission connected DSOs,


◾Significant grid users, i.e. All generating plants> 0.8 kW and consumers or aggregators with the possibility of affecting more than 50 MVA, as well as all consumers connected to the transmission network.


It contains regulations, inter alia. to:

◦Operation planning


◦Operational safety


◦Leistungs frequency control


◦Spannungs- / reactive power management


◦Kurzschlussleistung


◦Netzschutz


◦N-1 cases


◦Reserve management


◦TSO / DSO interface


The preliminary version is available here:

https://ec.europa.eu/energy/sites/ener/files/documents/SystemOperationGuideline%20final%28provisional%2904052016.pdf

Additional info: Also on 25 August the draft for the commentary of the German application AR 4141-1 appears

Technical rules for the operation and planning of network operators: Part1 - Interface transmission and distribution networks

Best regards,

◾TSOs,


◾Transmission connected DSOs,


◾Significant grid users, i.e. All generating plants> 0.8 kW and consumers or aggregators with the possibility of affecting more than 50 MVA, as well as all consumers connected to the transmission network.

******* DE
  >>> Erika Kämpf 8/14/2017 9:44 AM >>>
 Hallo zusammen,
die System Operation Guideline wird europaweit gelten und betrifft vor allem: 
◾TSOs, 
◾Transmission connected DSOs, 
◾Significant grid users, d.h. alle Erzeugungsanlagen > 0.8 kW und Verbraucher oder Aggregatoren mit der Möglichkeit mehr als 50 MVA zu beeinflussen, sowie alle an das Übertragungsnetz angeschlossenen Verbraucher.
Sie enthält Vorschriften u.a. zu:
◦Betrieblicher Planung
◦Betrieblicher Sicherheit
◦Leistungs-Frequenzregelung
◦Spannungs-/Blindleistungsmanagement
◦Kurzschlussleistung
◦Netzschutz
◦N-1 Fällen
◦Reserve-Management
◦TSO/DSO interface
Die vorläufige Fassung gibt es hier: 
https://ec.europa.eu/energy/sites/ener/files/documents/SystemOperationGuideline%20final%28provisional%2904052016.pdf
Zusatz-Info: Ebenfalls am 25. August erscheint der Entwurf zur Kommentierung der deutschen Anwendungsregel AR 4141-1 
Technische Regeln für den Betrieb und die Planung von Netzbetreibern: Teil1 – Schnittstelle Übertragungs- und Verteilnetze
Viele Grüße,
Erika
*** Transmission Line Rating
***** Thermal/Current Constraints
******* heat weakening
********* [[http://www.eia.doe.gov/cneaf/pubs_html/feat_trans_capacity/w_sale.html#textnote4][heating shortens life, can permanently stretch]]

          Thermal limitations are the most common constraints that limit the
          capability of a transmission line, cable, or transformer to carry
          power. The transmission line resists the flow of electrons through it,
          causing heat to be produced. The actual temperatures occurring in the
          transmission line equipment depend on the current, that is the rate of
          flow of the electrons, and also on ambient weather conditions, such as
          temperature, wind speed, and wind direction, because the weather
          effects the dissipation of the heat into the air. (4) The thermal
          ratings for transmission lines, however, are usually expressed in terms
          of current flows, rather than actual temperatures for ease of
          measurement.

          Thermal limits are imposed because overheating leads to two possible
          problems: (1) the transmission line loses strength because of
          overheating which can reduce the expected life of the line, and (2) the
          transmission line expands and sags in the center of each span between
          the supporting towers. If the temperature is repeatedly too high, an
          overhead line will permanently stretch and may cause its clearance from
          the ground to be less than required for safety reasons. Because this
          overheating is a gradual process, higher current flows can be allowed
          for limited time periods. A "normal" thermal rating for a line is the
          current flow level it can support indefinitely. Emergency ratings are
          levels the line can support for specific periods, for example, several
          hours.
********* caused by annealing: [[file:energy.bib::Daconti03incrPowTrans][Daconti & Lawry 2003: Increasing power transfer]]
********* annealing occurs at around 93C: [[http://portfolio.epri.com/ProgramTab.aspx%3FsId%3DPDU&rId%3D120&pId%3D4163&pjId%3D4169][EPRI: Impact of High-Temperature Operation on Conductor Systems - Project 38.005]]

***** Sag may not change w/ ambient air temp change of few degrees: [[http://www.sdfoundation.org/news/pdf/Focus2050_Technical%20Assesment.pdf][Climate Change Related Impacts in the San Diego Region by 2050]]

      However, it is conductor temperature (a function of load) that is the
      main cause of sagging power lines. Currently, there are insufficient
      data to conclude that ambient temperature increases of a few degrees
      would have a significant impact on line sag.

      A separate concern is line sag. As demand increases during hot weather, transmission
      line conductor temperatures increase, which causes the lines to stretch and sag. If a line sags
      into an object such as a tree, the current can be discharged to the ground, causing a short‐circuit
      36
      that could initiate a major power outage. However, it is conductor temperature (a function of
      load) that is the main cause of sagging power lines. Currently, there are insufficient data to
      conclude that ambient

*** Wildlife/Land Impacts
***** Bats
******* [[http://www.sciam.com/article.cfm%3Fid%3Dwind-turbines-kill-bats][Pressure drop kills bats]]
********* kills fewer birds (tougher lungs)
********* is worse for higher turbines
******* [[http://www.batsandwind.org/][Bats and Wind Energy Cooperative]] (BWEC, /lots of research/)
********* [[http://www.awea.org/windenergyweekly/WEW1320.html#Article1][press release]] (Iberdrola is a member)

          Ground-breaking environmental research. The Bats and Wind Energy
          Cooperative (BWEC), a government-industry-conservationist alliance
          including AWEA, Bat Conservation International, the U.S. Fish &
          Wildlife Service, and the National Renewable Energy Laboratory, began
          a landmark study at the Casselman wind farm in rural
          Pennsylvania. The project owner and operator, Iberdrola Renewables,
          is studying how changes to its operations during low wind conditions
          could help avoid bat deaths at the site. The study is the first of
          its kind in the U.S.

      models, it seems).

      - Radar @ Sea (National project / PSO)
      - SafeWind (EU)

*** [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/][Anemos.plus]]
***** [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dsection&id%3D14&Itemid%3D83][scientific & technical objectives]]:

      1. Enhanced Reliability, Ergonomy and Monitoring in Wind Power Forecasting Tools
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D44&Itemid%3D84][Following changing installed capacity]] is probably most important goal:
         - ringup for new farms
         - regional model upscale recalibration
      2. Operational Probabilistic Wind Power Forecasts
         Focus is on [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D45&Itemid%3D85][regional uncertainty]]
         - regional uncertainty models
         - regional prediction risk indices: "predicting predictability"
      3. Demonstration of New Operational Tools for Intelligent Power System Scheduling
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D46&Itemid%3D86][Focus is on small system stochastic unit commitment and economic dispatch]]
         - islands w/ wind high penetration
         - "maximise the expected social welfare subject to the constraints
           both deterministic and stochastic"
         - _multi-objective_ cost func.:robustness, reduction of operational costs, CO2 savings etc
         - better for Gianluca?
      4. Advanced Tools for Managing Secondary and Tertiary Reserves
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D47&Itemid%3D88][How much reserves do we need?]]
      5. Congestion Management in Large Power Systems as well as Local Grids
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D48&Itemid%3D89][connect the wind power forecasts to the load-flow calculations ]]
         - route power based on stochastics, not max power possible
         - prevent curtailments
         - just like Ariva T&D didn't want to do
         - related to [[Dynamic thermal ratings for wind power]]
      6. Decision Making Tools for Optimal Trading of Wind Power in Electricity Markets
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D49&Itemid%3D90][optimal bidding strategies]], accounting for storage, probabilistic
         forecasts, etc.
      7. Implement Tools for Optimal Coordination of Storage Options and Wind Power
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D50&Itemid%3D91][integration w/ hydro, pumped storage, etc.]] (v. similar to other objectives)
      8. An efficient methodology & advanced monitoring tools to quantify the benefits from large-scale wind integration
         [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D51&Itemid%3D92][How to evaluate wind integration success]]: CO2, security, money...
***** [[http://www.anemos-plus.eu/index.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content&view%3Dcategory&layout%3Dblog&id%3D56&Itemid%3D65][relevant papers]]
      - Pierre's scenarios paper: [[file:energy.bib::Pinson09probFrcstStatScenWind][Pinson et al. 2009: From]]
      - [[file:energy.bib::Chapados08augFrcstGaussProc][Chapados & Bengio 2008: Augmented Functional Time]] (could also use
        for scenarios)

*** Geothermal
***** Geothermal [[http://www1.eere.energy.gov/geothermal/future_geothermal.html][can provide 10%]] of US energy by 2050

      From [[http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/news/energy/2010/12/101228-geothermal-energy-pick-up-real-steam-/][here]]: Blackwell contributed to a broad study released in 2007 that
      predicted geothermal could provide one tenth of U.S. power by 2050. But
      that progress depends on new technology that can move geothermal beyond
      naturally occurring steam deposits. These enhanced geothermal systems
      would use tricks learned from oil and gas drilling. They would fracture
      rock with high-powered streams of water, generating steam to power
      turbines running above ground.

***** CA renewable plans using geothermal backup: [[file:energy.bib::Hart11genProfLrgVarRen][Hart & Jacobson 2011: Monte Carlo]]
***** Geothermal cost-efficient for up to 20% of CA C02 reductions: [[file:energy.bib::Hart12co2reduceRenew][Hart & Jacobson 2012]]: The carbon abatement potential of high penetration intermittent renewables
***** [[https://www.evernote.com/view/112a8f7a-e9b3-44d0-a8d4-98bd2562229f?locale%3Den_US#x%3Dtag:%2522geothermal%2520power%2522][Geothermal Energy’s Promise and Problems]]

* <<State Change Detection>>

  /Novelty/, /anomaly/, /outlier/, and /change-point/ detection are either synonymous or "closely related" (change-point), says [[cite:Pimentel14revNovDet][Pimentel et al. 2014]].  So his proposed classification is instead: 

  - probabilistic :: usually density estimation of /normal/" class
  - distance-based ::  dist based clustering, /normal/ data is tightly clustered
  - reconstruction based :: big regression model error ==> /novel/
  - domain based :: define a boundary around /normal/
  - information theoretic :: est. entropy, etc.: /novel/ data increases info content

******* R packages for change point detection

        Several almost-perfect packages here.  Several detect regression
        relationship changes, and some have time constraints on switching
        but it's not clear if they're learned Markov constraints or
        heuristics (I need to read more).

        segmented, strucchange and surveillance look most relevant.  Maybe msn?

********* [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/segmented/segmented.pdf][segmented]]: changes in (generalized) _multivariate regression models_
*********** *check it out*!
*********** quick test in [[file:~/proj/dongSpatTemp/segmented_test.R::##%20finding%20breakpoints%20by%20piecewise%20fitting][dongSpatTemp/segmented_test.R]]
*********** no Markov constraints
********* [[http://rgm2.lab.nig.ac.jp/RGM2/packages.php?show%3Dall&query%3Dpackage:strucchange][strucchange]]: structural changes in (linear) regression models
*********** overview paper: [[file:energy.bib::Kleiber02strucchange][Kleiber et al. 2002]]
*********** no Markov constraints
********* [[http://www.stat.uni-muenchen.de/~hoehle/pubs/hoehle_mazick2009-preprint.pdf][surveillance]]: changes in regression relationships
*********** main trick is that it detects state change _online_!
*********** based on statistical process control work
********* can derive predictive models from them
*********** can include periodicities
*********** Must do Markov since it depends on msm?
*********** Does somehow require more time to detect small changes
********* [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/msm/msm.pdf][msm:]] multistate markov
*********** markov constraint is good
*********** does hidden Markov but not the right kind

            is only [[http://www.stat.ucl.ac.be/ISdidactique/Rhelp/library/msm/html/msm.html][state + error]], where error is a misclassification prob.
            is apparently not a function of state _and_ covariates

*********** handles some kind of regression, maybe only on transition probls
            example: [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/msm/msm.pdf][cav data base]]:

            A series of approximately yearly angiographic examinations of
            heart transplant recipients. The state at each time is a grade
            of cardiac allograft vasculopathy (CAV), a deterioration of the
            arterial walls. _cav is a discrete variable with 4 values_

            format:
            A data frame containing 2846 rows. There are 622 patients, the
            rows are grouped by patient number and ordered by years after
            transplant, with each row representing an examination and
            containing additional covariates.

            *state* is the CAV number
            *inputs* are "additional covariates"

            Later, the coef.msm() Extract the estimated log transition
            intensities and the corresponding linear effects of each
            covariate. _Does this mean linear effects on transition?_

*********** monovariate, don't know if I like the angle thing...
********* [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/cumSeg/cumSeg.pdf][cumSeg:]] change in multivariate mean

********* [[http://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/bcp/bcp.pdf][bcp]]: Bayesian change in mean

*** <<Concept Drift Detection>>

    ie. recognizing that a new test or train point was not in previous
    training data. This would be a way to learn and store regimes

***** Gaussian process can warn when unfamiliar point in training data
******* [[file:energy.bib::Kocijan03caseCompNeuralGaussProc][Kocijan et al. 2003: Gaussian]] (also require less train data so fast)

*** TODO <<Covariance sparseness>>

    This is either sparseness by assuming a covariance parameterization or by some kind shrinkage or LASSO.  Either method may work on the covariance or precision matrix, and either may make spatio-temporal decomposition assumptions.

***** <<Covariance Matrix Parameterization>>

      Ways to constrain the values of a covariance matrix, reducing the number of parameters, and/or forcing empirical correlation estimates to yield a valid, positive definite covariance matrix.  These methods may work either on the covariance matrix or the precision matrix.

******* [[cite:Pinheiro96unCnstrParamVarCovMat][Pinheiro & Bates 1996: Unconstrained Cov. Mat Parameterizations]]
******* [[cite:Cai16strctHiDimCovPrecAdapt][Cai et al. 2016: Estimating structured high dim cov & prec matrices]]

******* [[cite:Tastu15spcTimeTrajGaussCpla][Tastu et al. 2015: Space Time Trajectories (precision matrix)]]

*** <<Non-stationary covariance>>

    Learning a covariance matrix that changes, conditionally on something.  By this, I don't mean "adaptive" but e.g. a wind power covariance matrix that is conditional upon wind speeds at different farms or a regional wind direction.

***** <<Basis projection for non-stationary covariance>>

      Could project copula inputs onto wind speed/power basis functions (like [[cite:Pinson04OonlinePredRiskWind][deterministic NWP speed/power forecasts]]) resulting in more meaningful covariance matrices (somehow?)

******* project inputs onto spline or fuzzy basis e.g. [[cite:Pinson04OonlinePredRiskWind][Pinson & Kariniotakis 2004]]
******* like [[file:energy.bib::Heim07spaceVaryCoeffs3D][Heim et al. 2007 3D space-varying coeffs p-spline tensor]] but for speed/power/(time lag or wind dir) 
******* then use [[cite:Li11tensoCovMatObjTrck][Li & Sun 2011: Tensor Covariance Matrix Obj Track]] ?
******* also [[Basis Learning]]

***** [[Varying coefficient models]]
***** Can [[Copula Processes]] do this? 
* <<Auto Machine Learning>> (autoML or "meta learning")
  Automatically tweaking machine learning parameters, selecting algorithms, feature selection, outlier detection, ensemble building, etc.  A new field I discovered at ECML PKDD 2017
*** [[cite:Feurer15autoMLautoSkLrn][Feurer et al. 2015: Efficient Robust Automated Machine Learning]] (code: auto-sklearn)
*** Also [[Frugal Machine Learning]]
* <<Frugal Machine Learning>>

  At the ECML PKDD 2017 roundtable discussion, one of the researchers mentioned this area, as the place where academic researchers can make progress even if they don't have Google's gigantic computers.  I googled for the topic immediately after the conference but didn't see an overview paper or website, but did get some seeemingly related hits:

*** [[http://repository.tue.nl/855430][Frugal learning Masters Thesis: Frugality score]]

    A way of ranking algorithms by accuracy vs. frugalty.  Master's Thesis by, I think one of the students of the main speakers at ECML PKDD 2017 (Joaquin Vanschoren).

*** R package: [[https://cran.r-project.org/web/packages/FFTrees/vignettes/guide.html][FFTrees: Fast-and-frugal decision trees]]
*** [[cite:Laskey14fastFrugalTreesVsBayesNetsRisk][Laskey & Martignon 2014: Fast Frugal Trees vs. Bayes Net Risk Assessmnt]]
*** [[https://www.nsf.gov/awardsearch/showAward?AWD_ID=1652131][NSF Award Search: Award 1652131-CAREER: Hashing and Sketching Algorithms for Resource-Frugal Algorithms]]
*** Also [[Auto Machine Learning]]

* <<My optimization learning path>>
  Stuff I should learn about for electricity system optimization

  *Overall approach (thinking as of May 11, 2014)*

  /Start with Convex optimization/
  o this means starting w/t linear programming?
    e.g. Juan Mi's stoch elec. systems class requires linear programming
  o convex opt is a superset of linear programming (and course reviews it)
  o convex opt is a better way to do nonlinear QR, maybe QR variable selection
  o 2nd Convex opt class (EE364b) does robust optimization (but so does MIT
    linear programming cours)
  o stochastic programming covered in EE34b lecture 5
  o Convex opt. is a prereq. for submodular opt course (Bilmes)
  o submodular opt is the new convex opt.
  o if I get lost in Convex opt. class, go back to MIT book (which I have
    already bought) and the MIT class

*** Convex optimization

    *Conclusion*: start w/ [[CVX101 Convex Optimization Winter 2014]]
                (videos, quizzes, [[https://class.stanford.edu/courses/Engineering/CVX101/Winter2014/info][Matlab]], etc.) and then try EE364b

***** Why
******* Convex optimization is a generalization of linear programming

/From Boyd's (Standford teacher) [[www.stanford.edu/~boyd/cvxbook/bv_cvxbook.pdf][course book]] introduction/ (p. 2)

Comparing (1.3) and (1.2), we see that convexity is more general than
linearity: inequality replaces the more restrictive equality, and the
inequality must hold only for certain values of α and β. Since any linear
program is therefore a convex optimization problem, we can consider convex
optimization to be a generalization of linear programming.

******* Convex optimization used for nonlinear QR
        See [[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MM_algorithm][MM algorithm on Wikipedia]], and the mmqr.m algorithm contributed
        [[http://sites.stat.psu.edu/~dhunter/code/qrmatlab/][here]].  Also see: [[file:energy.bib::Hunter00qrMMalg][Hunter & Lange 2000: Quantile MM]] (technote and slides)
      o the MM algorithm is another [[http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2674769/][way to do variable selection]]
